RULES FOR WHEN TO FAST
ekādaśī ca sampūrnā viddheti dvividhā smrtā I99  viddhā ca dvividhā tatra tyājyā viddhā tu pūrvajā
Ekādaśī is known as either full or mixed. There are also two  kinds of mixed Ekādaśīs, of which the one mixed with the previous should be avoided.
DDT: The Ekādaśī that is mixed with Daśamī, the previous tithi, should be avoided. That means one should not  fast on it.
Now, the Purāna-samuccaya and others say: `O king,  those desiring liberation should fast on the pure Dvādaśī,  but materialistic householders should without a doubt  fast on the Ekādaśī that is mixed with the previous:  These statements are rejected.
(200-336  In the Garuda Purāna:`If the sunrise touches even a fraction of 337
the Daśamī, then on that Ekādaśī Vaisnavas should not fast:  DEFINITION OF A VAISNAVA  grhīta-visnu-dīksāko visnu-sevā-paro narah 338
vaisnavas cātra samgrāhyah skāndādy-uktānusāratah  According to the statements of the Skanda Purāna and other  authorities, a man who has taken initiation into a Visnu-mantra  and is devoted to serving Visnu is to be accepted as a Vaisnava.
DDT: Who then is a Vaisnava? Fearing that someone  might ask whether a Vaisnava is one who has devotion to  the Lord or someone else, he writes this verse. These  rules pertain to such a person, but not to those who have  attained full faith in the path of devotion, since they do
not have to follow vratas and the like. This should be understood later also, when the rules of avoiding things  such as brass utensils on Dvādaśī and other days are described.
339-340 About this, in the Skanda Purāna: `One who never gives up  Ekādaśī, whether in the greatest misfortune or in a happy situation, his determination is Vaisnava. Who is equal to all living beings, who does not deviate from his own duties and whose all actions are connected with Lord Visnu, he is known as a Vaisnava.'
DDT: He is equal to all living beingś because he is not  violent and does not criticise, but treats everyone as he  would himself.'His own duties' refer to Vaisnava-dharma.
34I And in the Padma Purāna: `Those who follow rules of initiation, who have nyāsas and yantras and who meditate on a  twelve- or eight-syllabled mantra, or some other, and who are  attached to the worship of Visnu, are known as Vaisnavas:
DDT: Nyāsas and yantras are parts of the worship.`Some  other' refers to mantras such as the Srī Gopāla-mantra.  Since worship cannot be fruitful without initiation, initiation is also implied here. Of all initiated those attached  to the worship of Visnu are specified.
(342-4I3)  HOW TO RESOLVE DOUBTS  WHETHER OR NOT TO FAST
414 Śrī Brahmā says in the Visnu-rahasya: `The words and deeds  of those who always serve Visnu with their minds, words and  bodies, should be known as equal to Visnu:
DDT: If there is doubt because of a dispute between many  different astrologers and knowers of scripture, it should  be resolved by the statements of those devoted to the  Lord, not by others. Serving'with their minds, words and  bodies' means by remembrance, glorification, circumambulation and so on.
The Lord says in the Kūrma Purāna: `One should ask the 4i5-4r6  Vaisnava brāhmanas, conversant with the Vaisnava scriptures,
firm in their vratas and of pure behaviour, and then zealously  follow their advice: In the Padma Purāna, Vaisnava-tantra:  'The statements of those who know the Itihāsas and Puranās,  are acquainted with the conclusion of the Smrtis and who are  dear to Vāsudeva, are Vedic:
WHAT TO AVOID
In the Visnu-rahasya and Kūrma Purāna:'Statements not based 4y-4i9  on the authority of the Uedas, brāhmanas, Janārdana, Tantras or
the Dharma-śāstras, should be rejected: In the Vaisnava-tantra:  `Statements of those who have no devotion to the guru, uttering mantras or the supersoul, Visnu, should always be rejected: In the Skanda Purāna:`Statements of those who do not  have devotion to the Lord of all, Visnu, the most auspicious,  should not be accepted if one desires the perfection of one's religious endeavour.'
DDT: `The most auspiciouś can also mean 'or to Srī  Rudra:
And also: `The statements of men who blaspheme the Pañca- 42o-42t  rātras, Purānas and Itihāsas should certainly be rejected: Yajña
valkya also says: `The Purānas, Pañcarātras, Vedas and Pāśupatas are most authoritative. They should not be contradicted:  DDT:'Not contradicted' means not disputed through arguments based on false logic.
Thus ends the twelfth Vilāsa, called `Description of Ekādaśī',  in the Śrī Bhagavad-bhakti-viLāsa, written by Srī Gopāla Bhatta.




VILĀSA XIII  CELEBRATING THE VISNU-VRATA
HOW TO PERFORM EKADAŚI  AND MAHA-DVADAŚI  INVOCATION
vande caitanya-devam tam krsnam nitya-navotsavam 1  yasya prasādāt sidhyanti dīnasyāpi mahotsavāh
I worship Lord Caitanya, Krsna, the eternally fresh festival, by  whose mercy celebrations of even the fallen are successful.  DIG-DARŚINI-TIKA:
yasya śaktyāmśalābhena brahmāder api śaktayah  tās tā vibhānti tam vande sarva-śakti-pradam vibhum
I worship the Almighty, the bestower of all power, by a  fraction of whose power the powers of Brahmā and the  others glimmer.
Having described the Ekādaśī-vrata the author will  now discuss the celebration beginning at Daśamī. To accomplish the celebration of writing that, he worships the  Lord with this verse. The Lord is an eternally fresh festival for the devotees, or then His form is a festival of fresh  characteristics.
RULES FOR THE DAY BEFORE THE FAST  prātah-snānādikan krtvā suveśo dhauta-vastrakah 2  vratam sañkalpya kurvīta vaisnavaiś ca mahotsavam
Having taken their morning bath, etc, well dressed in fresh  clothes and having declared the vrata, the Vaisnavas should  perform the celebration.
DDT: `Etć means having performed all their morning duties such as sandhya-vandana. They should be `well dressed' by following the regulation for shaving, etc, for Vaisnavas on Daśamī. The unfavorable time for shaving is  given in the Ratna-mālā: `By those who have given up eating and unguents, have gone outside their villages or who  follow a vow, no shaving should be done on Navamī, the  ninth day. At initiation, release from prison, preparing for  death and marriage, on the order of the king and by brāhmanas: in all these cases the seers have declared shaving  auspicious: And also in the Smrti: `Hot water, unguents,  sleeping, shaving and sex: these should zealously be avoided on the three days beginning with Daśamī: This should  be understood as pertaining to non-Vaisnavas.
One should perform the celebration as has been described and as will be described further on, naturally always  behaving well. In particular, one should prepare the temple  of the Lord by cleaning it and so on, decorating it with banners and Aags, and then happily place the Lord on a beautiful throne. Then one should offer great worship with devotion, invite the Vaisnavas and respectfully sing and dance.
THE MANTRA OF DECLARATION  3 daśamī-dinam ārabhya karisye 'ham vratam tava
tridinam deva-deveśa nirvighnam kuru keśava  `Beginning on the day of Daśamī, I will perform a three-day vrata  for you, Lord of the god of gods. Remove all obstacles, Keśava!'
4 Even if the performer touches something untouchable he  should not bathe. In the Visnu-smrti: `He who, fearing impurity, bathes on the festival of Vāsudeva becomes impure. Anyone who sees him should enter water with all his clothes on!'  5 stutvātha bahudhā krsnarri ghosayen niyamānvitam
śrīrukmāńgada-mattebha- patahodghositam vacah
After one has praised Krsna in many ways one should proclaim the rules to be followed with words thundering like a  kettledrum on Śrī Rukmārigada's ferocious elephant.
DDT: During the festival one should in many ways  praise Krsna by hymns in prose and poetry. One should  proclaim the rules loudly and listen to them. `The rules'  means the rules for Daśamī, etc, which will be explained  further on.
About this it is said in the Nārada Purāna (2.23.32-34):`People! On the beginning of the day of Hari, stay at home and eat  only once. The food should be without ksāra and consist of  havisya. Sleeping on the ground and giving up the company of  your loved ones, remember God, the master, the most ancient,  highest person! Also on Dvādaśī you should only eat once:
And also:`To have sex with your mother is good. To eat the 8  Aesh of cows is good. To kill or to drink wine is also good, but  not to eat on Ekādaśī:
KSARA  Cereals, except mung-beans and sesame-seeds; beans; wheat 9  and kodrava (Perpelum Scrobiculatum); chickpeas and devagrains (Andropogon Saccharatus): this group is known as ksāra.
HAVISYA  Husked white winter rice, mung-beans and sesame, kalāya 10-13  beans, pigweed (Enastrus Paniculatus), vāstūka (Chenopodium  Album), sastika, jute (Corchorus Capsularis), radish, root bulbs
except taro (Colocasia Antiquorum), Sind- or sea-salt, gavya yoghurt, ghee, unskimmed milk - breadfruit (jackfruit), mango,  yellow myrobalan (Terminalia Chebula), pepper, cumin, ginger,  tamarind, banana, carambola (Averrhoa Acida), Indian gooseberry (Emblica Officinalis), sugar without molasses, all cooked  without oil: this the seers call havisya.
DDT: Sastika is a kind of quickly growing rice, or then a  kind of leafy vegetable.
OTHER PROHIBITIONS
14 In the Skanda Purāna: 'Brass utensils, meat, masura-beans,  honey, speaking lies, eating more than once and physical labour should be avoided on Daśamī:
DDT: In some readings'physical labour' is replaced with  overeating. That alternative is also acceptable.
15-16 In the Kūrma Purāna:`Brass utensils, meat, masura-beans, chickpeas, kodrava, leafy vegetables, honey, women and eating other  peopleś food should be avoided.` And also:'Brass utensils, meat,  masura-beans, eating more than once, sex, gambling and drinking much water: these seven should be avoided on Daśamī:
17 In the Matsya Purāna: `Brass, meat, wine, honey, oil, lies,  physical exertion, absence from home, sleeping in the daytime,  sex, stoneground flour and masura-beans: these should be given  up on Dvādaśī:
DDT: Earlier (4.130) it was said that when one bathes on  Daśamī one should certainly use oil. `He who bathes  without oil on Daśamī is ignorant: Here oil has been  prohibited within the rules for Daśamī, but there is no  contradiction, since there are different rules for materialists and desireless persons. This can be seen from the  continuation of the quoted passage: `His life, intellect,  fame and strenght are all four destroyed: In this way contradictions should be resolved elsewhere also.
18 In another Smrti: `On Daśamī he who eats only once should,  controlling the senses, do ācamāna and then use a twig for brushing the teeth:
THE GREATNESS OF DAŚAMI
19-21 In the Brahma-vaivarta Purana:`When one scrapes his tongue  with a tooth-twig on Daśamī in order to follow the rules of Dvādaśī, Yama loses hope. Dejected, he destroys the sin that has  been recorded. The sinner who does not eat goes to the abode
of Visnu. To eat in the middle of the day according to the rules  is called"eating oncé', and it should be zealously performed:
DDT: After eating on Daśamī one should clean oneś  teeth with a twig. On Ekādaśī twigs of palāśa (Butea  Frondosa) and other trees are forbidden. As it is said:'On  Ekādaśī one should clean the mouth by only rinsing with  water twelve times:
tato rātrim nayetāñ ca brahmacārī jitendriyah za  bhagavantam smaran bhaktyā bhūmiśāyī sukham svapan
Then at night one should as a brahmacārī, with controlled  senses, remember the Lord with devotion and happily sleep on  the ground.
DDT: As a brahmacārī' means giving up the company of  women, etc. It has already been written that one should  refrain from sex, so here `as a brahmacārí should be understood as not looking at women, and so on. That will be  made clear further on (í3.5z).
RULES FOR THE DAY OF FASTING
prātah snātvārcayitvā ca bhagavantam yathāvidhi 23  tārnra-pātrariv samādāya vrata-samkalpam ācaret
After having bathed in the morning and worshipped the Lord  according to the rules, one should fetch a copper vessel and state  the declaration.
DDT: According to the rules' means as has been explained earlier on in the book (Vilāsas 3-9).
About this Devala says: `Having fetched a copper vessel filled z4  with water, the wise should, facing the north, start the fast or  state the declaration:
DDT: If there is no copper vessel one may simply state  the declaration.
THE MANTRA OF DECLARATION  25 ekādaśyām nirāhārah sthitvāhwm apare 'hani
bhoksyāmi pundarīkāksa śaranam me bhavācyuta
`O lotus-eyed one, I will remain fasting on Ekādaśī and eat on  the next day. O Acyuta, please be my shelter!'
26 uccārayann imam mantram śrīkrsna-caranābjayoh  puspāñjalim samarpyātha mantra-pūtam jalam pibet  Uttering this mantra one should offer a handful of flowers to  the lotus feet of Srī Krsna. Then one should drink the mantraconsecrated water.
27-28 About this Mārkāndeya says: `He who desires the fruit of  the fast should concentratedly drink water consecrated by  muttering the eight-syllabled mantra three times over it. Having worshipped God and offered a handful of flowers, he should  utter the mantra of declaration and announce it to God:
DDT: After worshipping the Lord it is sometimes said  that one should drink to his satisfaction and sometimes  that one should offer a handful of flowers. There is an option between either drinking water or offering flowers  here. In another reading an option between worshipping  and offering flowers is also indicated.
29 daśamyām cārddha-rātropary anuvrttau purah-sarān  ekādaśyāś catur yāmān hitvā sańkalpam ācaret
If Daśamī extends beyond midnight, one should wait until  twelve hours of the Ekādaśī have passed before uttering the  declaration.
30-32 About this is also said: `When midnight is touched by  Daśamī one should give up the first twelve hours of the  Ekādaśī with regard to worship and the declaration: And in  the Nārada Purāna (2.z.t5-2o): `O brāhmana, when there is  the fault of connection with the earlier day, one should avoid  bathing and worship during the first twelve hours of the
Ekādaśī. Afterwards those who fast should bathe, worship  and so on. If the duties of the day are not completed, then the  night is allotted. The duties of the day should be completed at  the beginning of night:
tataś ca bhagavad-bhaktyā paricaryādi-rūpayā 33  dinam rātriñ cagamayed upavāsa paro budhah
Then the intelligent person, devoted to the fast, should spend  the day and night in devotion to the Lord by worship and so  forth.
About this, in the Skanda Purāna: `The intelligent one 34  should, having worshipped the Lord of the god of gods with
the greatest devotion, pass the day and night to attain the fruit  of the fasting.'
DEFINITION OF FASTING
In the Grha-pariśista, Kātyāyana-smrti, Visnu-dharma, Brah- 35  ma-vaivarta Purāna, etc:`To stand fast in the face of sin by cultivating good qualities, and to give up all enjoyment, is called  fasting.'
ENJOYMENT  It is said by Śātātapa: `Perfumes, ornaments, fine clothes, flo- 36-37  wer garlands, ointments, brushing the teeth and cosmetics
pollute one during a fast, and by Srī Vyāsa:`Flowers, ornaments,  fine clothes, sandalwood, incense, ointments, brushing the  teeth and cosmetics defile one during a fast:
DDT: Here he lists the items of enjoyment. `Cosmetics'  means that which actors, etc, use in their eyes. These  things are polluting during a fast and should therefore be  avoided. That is the implied meaning.
In the Kāśi-khanda of the Skanda Purāna it is however said:`Even during a day of fasting brushing the teeth  and cosmetics do not corrupt.` This mainly refers to the
dress of women, where using cosmetics is an integral part. In the same way the other things, such as brushing the teeth, in that verse should be understood as pertaining to women. This has been explained earlier in the book (á.22q-zzó).
SIN 38-39 Srī Sumantu says:`Not observing the rules, not restraining the senses and performing forbidden worship should always be diligently avoided: As said by Śātātapa: `Speaking lies, gambling, sleeping at day and sex: a man devoted to the fast should do none of these during Ekādaśī:
4o-4r And in the Visnu-dharma: `Those who fast and are devoted to the worship of Visnu should not touch heretics or speak with them: In the Srī Visnu Purāna (3.18.97): `Therefore, the disciple should give up speaking with or touching sinful heretics especially at the time of sacrifies, and so on:
42-43 The atonement for that has been mentioned: After seeing such a person the wise should look at the sun: Also, in the Visnu-dharma: After touching, the wise becomes pure after bathing and looking at the sun. After speaking with them, he should think of Acyuta who dwells in purity.'
DDT: It is understood by this that one should avoid even seeing such people.`Who dwells in purity' means that He is situated in pure water or in pure motives.
GOOD QUALITIES
44-45 In the Bhavisya Purāna: `Patience, truthfulness, mercy, silence, purity, control of the senses, worship of the Lord, sacrificial libations, satisfaction and refraining from stealing: this tenfold dharma is common for all vratas.` In the Padma Purāna, in a conversation between Yama and Dhūmraketu: `Having restrained himself on Daśamī, he should pass the day of the vrata with controlled senses, without anger or violence and praising Krsna:
DDT: First he gives the common good qualities and then writes about the special good quality on Ekādaśī with the second quotation. Though one could say that controlling the senses, etc, belong to the common good qualities, it can be said to be special because of the special performer. `Praising Krsná means to perform Krsna-kīrtana. One should pass the day like this. This is the main rule.
In the Visnu-dharmottara: `To utter His mantra, meditate on 46 His mantra, listen to stories about Him, worship Him and to praise and hear His names, etc: these qualities are mentioned
by the thoughtful to be followed during a fast:
DDT:'Etć refers to the different modes of devotion, such as praying.
THE GREATNESS OF THE FAST
It is said in the Visnu-dharma: `The man who fasts and meth- 47 tates with devotion upon Hari, who utters His mantras, who performs His work, whose mind is attached to Him, without desires, without a doubt attains the abode of Brahman, just
like the demon:
DDT:'Without desireś means that he has no desires, or then that even if he has, he becomes desireless. The abode consisting of Brahman is Śrī Vaikuntha. `The demoń is Srī Prahlāda.
OTHER RULES FOR THE DAY OF FASTING
In the Kātyāyana-smrti:'One should fast fully, observing brah- 48-49 macārya: Devala says: `Brahmacārya, non-violence, truthful
ness and vegetarianism: these four should always be practised during vratas:
DDT: Vegetarianism should be practised on the day of fasting and when breaking the fast. Though it was said with the verse 'these eight things do not break a vratá (iz.ioo) that medicine does not break the vrata, medicine
in the form of meat should be avoided. This is also said by  Vyāsa: `One should always avoid meat on the day of fasting and when breaking the fast, even if it is in the form of  medicine:
50-51 And also:`By repeatedly drinking water, by chewing betel once,  by sleeping in the daytime and by sex the fast is destroyed:  Moreover: `By brushing one's teeth, betel, sleeping in the daytime, by sex and by repeatedly drinking water one will not attain the fruit of the fast:
THINGS THAT BREAK BRAHMACARYA  5z About this it has been said:`By looking at women, by touching  them or speaking with them, brahmacārya is destroyed, but  not by timely union with one's wife.`
DDT: Brahmacārya is not destroyed by looking, etc, at  one's own wife, but by intercourse. This is the real meaning.  DUTIES OF THE EVENING
53 tato nityārcannriv krtvā hari ghasrotsavārthikām  krtvā sāyam mahāpūjārń kūryāj jāgaranam niśi
Then, having performed the mandatory service on the festival  on the day of Hari, one should perform great worship in the  evening and then keep vigil at night.
THE WORSHIP
54-59 In the Brahmā Purāna:`Best of seers, one should attentively and  with faith construct an excellent mandala of different flowers  around the Lord: And also (z28.í-5): `One should attentively  fast on Ekādaśī during both fortnights. Having bathed according to the rules one should, dressed in pure clothes and  with controlled senses, correctly with faith and very attentively  worship Visnu with flowers, sandalwood, incense, lights, food
offerings, many other articles - such as uttering mantras, sacrifices, and circumambulations - hymns, different dances,  songs and recitations pleasing to the Lord, stick-like obeisances and loud shouts of`Jaya!". After worshipping like this following the rules, one should keep vigil at night. He who is devoted to Visnu should recite narrations or sing. That man will  go to the supreme dwelling of Visnu. There is no doubt about it:
In the Bhavisya Purāna:`Having worshipped Hari one should 60  pass the night following Ekādaśī as one is able by listening to the  Purānas and so forth:
DESCRIPTION OF THE VIGIL
vaisnavān jāgare 'bhyarccya tīrtham śańkhodakānvitam 61  tebhyo dattvā svayam prāśya vidvān stotrādikam pathet
After worshipping the Vaisnavas during the vigil, the wise should  o$ér them holy water together with water from a conchshell and  then drink it himself. Then he should read hymns and so forth.
purānādi tatah śrutvā gītā-nrtyādika¥ svayam 62  kuryāt paśyec ca pārakya¥ vārayen na hasen na ca
After hearing scriptures such as the Purānas, one should himself sing and dance and also watch others do that. One must  not hinder or laugh at this singing and dancing!
THE PROHIBITION AGAINST  HINDERING SINGING AND SO  FORTH DURING THE VIGIL
In the Padma Purāna: `He who obstructs song or dance during 63-64  the vigil of Hari boils for 60 000 yugas in Raurava and other
hells. He who laughs, etc, at a dancing man during the vigil goes  to hell until fourteen Indras have passed:
THE NECESSITY OF SEEING THE VIGIL
65 In the Skanda Purāna: `Yama presents such a person with hell and great torture. One should not even look at a face that has not seen the vigil:
DDT: It was said that one should`watch others` (í3.6Z). With this and the following verses he shows that seeing the vigil is mandatory. `Presentś means that Yama will take him from his sinful bed and very angrily, with curved eyebrows and with contempt take him away.
66-68 And also: `Those beings who do not see the vigil of Hari will indeed have their eyes ripped out and get kicked in the chest: Furthermore: `Those whose eyes are bright with the fire of Kali never see the vigil of Krsna, and never Janārdana.' Also: `The eyes of men who do not see the vigil are sinful. They are firmly surrounded by the many prominent sins of Kali:
RULES FOR THE VIGIL
69-73 In the Skanda Purāna, a conversation between Brahmā and Nārada (2.4.6.r-5):`Listen Nārada! I will speak about the characteristics of the vigil. Even with only a little knowledge about them, Janārdana is easy to attain. Song, music, dance, reading the Purānas; offering incense, lamps, foodstuffs, flowers, sandalwood-paste, fruits and water; faith, charity, sense-control, truthfulness, refraining from sleep, cheerfulness, observance of the rules, showing astonishment and enthusiasm, refraining from sin and laziness and so forth, performing circumambulations and obeisances, lighting lamps and happiness of mind: O fortunate one, with all these things one should perform ārātrika of Hari every third hour.'
DDT: The words`and so forth' in after`refraining from sin and laziness' refer to gambling, gossiping, etc. The most important quality is happiness of mind. Refraining from sin and laziness are reckoned as two different things,
which brings the list up to 26 different things, as stated in another reading.
And also (2.q.33.í6-z7):`He who performs this vigil on the day of 74-75 Visnu with devotion and without wickedness of mind merges in
the Supersoul. A rich man who however does the vigil deceitfully will himself then be tricked by a vile gambler.'
DDT: The vigil should be done without deceit, as is shown by these two verses first positively and then negatively. `Mergeś means that he attains eternal, close proximity.
In the same book, a conversation between Umā and Maheś- 76-78 vara: `Following the scriptures, refraining from sleep, dancing,
singing, music, clapping of hands, lights, company of saints, offerings of articles, well-known symptoms of devotion, satisfaction, happiness and delighting the people: with these twelve one should diligently perform the vigil dear to Mādhava during both the light and dark fortnight:
Moreover: `Criticising others, having a disturbed mind, 79-8r not following the scriptures, not singing, not lighting lamps,
not offering articles even though able to do so, indifference and sleeping: a vigil with these nine qualities suitable for Kali is particularly low' And also: `Instead of speaking one should sing and dance. O Durgā, when speaking, one should read the Purānas:
THE MANDATORINESS OF THE VIGIL
In the Skanda Purāna, a conversation between Brahmā and 82-84 Nārada (7.4.28.47-49): `If someone does not keep vigil on the
day of Visnu, then his previous and coming relatives will be cast down. By non-performance he destroys his sons, merit and wealth. A residence in hell is created for him with his ancestors for a long time. O best of brāhmanas, this sin will not be destroyed by atonement, vratas or deep meditation without the vigil on Dvādaśī:
DDT: Since the vigil is necessary for even destroying sin,  its mandatoriness is proven.
85-86 In the same book, a conversation between Umā and Maheśvara:` The fortune of one who does not keep vigil on the day of  Visnu is destroyed just like by insulting Vaisnavas. He will not  have any interest in the vigil of Dvādaśī, and he will not have  eligibility for worshipping Keśava:
87 In the same book Brahmā says: `In whose heart Hari, the  Lord of yoga, always resides, in him interest in the vigil on Dvādaśī is born:
MANDATORINESS OF  SINGING, ETC, DURING THE VIGIL  88 sāmānyena purālekhi gīta-vādyādi-nityatā
adhunā likhyate so yam jāgare ca viśesatah
Previously the mandatoriness of singing, dancing and so on  was discussed in a general sense. Now this will be described in  connection with the vigil.
DDT: In connection with the vigil he now again writes  about the mandatoriness of song, dance and so on, a  mandatoriness he has already established with regard to  the daily duties (8.z5í-a95). Fearing the fault of repetition, he writes this verse. The intended meaning is that  one should certainly sing, dance and so on during the  vigil. And so on' refers to uttering hymns, etc.
89-9o In the Skanda Purāna, a conversation between Umā and Maheśvara: `He who like a dumb person does not read or sing on the  vigil of Hari will be born into dumbness in seven births. O  Pārvatī, the fool who does not dance during the vigil of Hari  will be born into lameness in seven births:
91-92 In the Padma Purāna, in connection with the Paksavardhinī-vrata: `Those people who do not praise or appreciate the  vigil of Hari will have no festivals in their houses during seven
births. Those who praise and extol the vigil of the Carrier of  the disk will have a continous festival for fifteen births!'
THE GREATNESS OF THE VIGIL
In the Skanda Purāna, a conversation between Brahmā and 93-94  Nārada, and in the Prahlāda-samhitā:'The ancestors will not
attain liberation by offerings at Gayā, nor by sacrifices at many  holy places without the vigil on Dvādaśī. In whatever situation, one who performs the vigil of Hari on Dvādaśī with every  three hours burns sins from a thousand lives.
`O brāhmana, one who offers a lamp during the vigil of the 95-98  night of Hari attains the fruit of giving away a hundred cows
with every blink of the eye. One who performs worship of  Hari with flowers during the vigil of Dvādaśī attains the fruit  of a horse-sacrifice with every flower. One who burns aloe-incense after worshipping Visnu during the vigil attains the fruit  of giving away a hundred plates of sesame-seeds with each half  of an eyeblink. O twice-born one, one who burns bdellium-incense with ghee for just a moment during the vigil of Hari attains the fruit one would normally attain after a whole month.
DDT: After a whole month' means that burning bdellium  with ghee during the vigil gives the same fruit as burning  it during a whole month otherwise. Another reading of  the text has'the fruit of the month of Māghá meaning the  fruit one attains by bathing, etc, during that month.
`One who offers Visnu food made of havisya during the vigil 99-101  attains the merit of offering a mountain of rice. One who offers
cooked preparations and different fruits during the vigil of  Padmanābha again attains the fruit of giving away ten thousand cows. One who offers betel with camphor during the vigil  as a gift to Padmanābha will live in Śvetadvīpa for a long time.
`One who constructs a flower mandala during the vigil of 102-104  Padmanābha will sport with flower airplanes in the abode of
Brahmā. One who burns aguru with camphor on the vigil of
Padmanābha burns sins from a hundred thousand lives. O twiceborn one, one who bathes Krsna with yoghurt, milk, ghee and so  on during the night of the vigil will indeed partake of liberation.
105-108 `One who offers divine garments on the vigil will be splendid for as many manvantaras as there are threads in the cloth.  One who offers Visnu ornaments made of gold and jewels will  live with me for seven kalpas. He is certainly dear to me. O  best of sages, one who, in the age of Kali, offers pure sandalwood, camphor, aloe and keśara together with musk on the vigil  of Hari without a doubt attains the fruit of a horse-sacriñce  for each one by the mercy of Vāsudeva.
109-113 `One who burns a lamp with excellent ghee before Visnu  on the night of the vigil achieves the fruit of donating ten  thousand cows in a moment. One who burns a camphor-lamp  on the vigil of Vāsudeva attains the fruit of donating ten million brown cows. One who performs ārātrika with camphor  on the vigil gains liberation together with ten thousand relatives. On the vigil of Hari even ārātrika without camphor or  the donation of a poor man will give a great fruit. One who  bathes the head of Hari with water in a conch-shell will carry  on his head the fruit of bathing in the Gangā.
114-116 After worshipping Hari during the vigil, one who is already clean should read the Visnu-sahasra-nāma, the Gītā, the  liberation of the elephant, the auspicious bathing and Vedic  chants again and again with devotion. By reading during the  vigil before Hari, the form of sacriñce, one attains the merit of  donating a hundred red cows for every syllable.
117-119 `Then again, the merit of one who sings, dances and plays  music cannot be attained through a hundred sacrifices or a  hundred vratas or donations. He who sings and dances even  though shy will achieve the fruit of the dharma of the four  āśramas. On the vigil of Padmanābha one should read from a  book. One will stay in heaven near Visnu for as many yugas as  there were ślokas in the book.
120-122 `One who decorates the altar with beautiful banana-trunks  and mango-leaves on the vigil of the Cakra-bearer will have a
festival in heaven for as many yugas as there were leaves. He  will be worshipped by Indra and others, and surrounded by  apsarās he will enjoy. If some of those who dance on the vigil  go to hell, they will be freed by Dharmarāja and then proceed  to the feet of Hari, to liberation.
`The lord of Ramā is pleased by the sound of singing on the 123-125  vigil. He will bestow happiness superior to that enjoyed by

DDT: `Yogá means the eightfold system. `Samkhyá  means knowledge of the self.

140-144 `O brāhmana, it is certainly known that many persons  previously attained liberation by satisfying Visnu on the  vigil, just like a dog-eater once did by singing. THE FAULT OF NOT  PERFORMING THE VIGIL
171-172 In the Skanda Purāna, in a conversation between Umā and  Maheśvara (x.5.23.8-4.2): `Those who sleep on the day of the  killer of Madhu are bitten by the serpent of Kali. Those who  do not perform the vigil are bound by the web of māyā. Those
who do not perform the vigil on Ekādaśī in the age of Kali are  ruined. There is no doubt about it. Therefore their lives are  unsure.
`O Gaurī, the merit of a thousand horse-sacrifices and ten 173-177  thousand times ten million Vājapeya-offerings is not equal to
that of the vigil of Visnu. Beautiful one, when the vigil of Hari  has been performed, the family of the father, mother and wife  is promoted. When people perform the vigil on the pure day  of Visnu, Hari becomes delighted and dances amongst them!  For as many days as one performs the vigil of Hari in front of  Keśava, so many tens of thousands of yugas one will stay in the  abode of Visnu. However, for as many days as one does not  perform the vigil, the servants of Yama will dance in one's house  with raised weapons.
`One who reads the Purānas on the vigil of Vāsudeva will 178-181  attain his desired goals. He will not become a ghost. One who
again sings and dances on the vigil of Hari attains the abode of  Brahmā, my abode and indeed that of Visnu. Furthermore, the  Vaisnava who illuminates the directions on the vigil of Visnu  will dwell in Vaikuntha forever with his ancestors. The man  who puts his mind to the vigil of Hari will dwell in Svetadvīpa  for sixty thousand years.
`Pārvatī! Whatever sins people commit in ten million lives, 182-184  all those are burnt on the vigil of Krsna. Those who perform
the vigil in front of a Sālagrāma-stone will attain the fruit of  ten million Cāndrāyana-sacrifices with every three hours. One  cannot attain enjoyment, wealth, sons, fame or an eternal  abode by ten thousand sacrifices without the vigil on Dvādaśī.
`Every step a pilgrim takes towards the temple of Keśava on 185-188  the vigil equals a horse-sacriñ_ce! The wanderer will stay in
heaven for as many thousands of years as the times he bows  down to the earth on the vigil. Therefore, in the age of Kali, in  order to destroy sin, one should leave his house on the vigil of  the twelve Dvādaśīs and go to a temple of Mādhava. What is  the use of many strict vratas or living in a holy place if one does  not peform the vigil when the day of Dvādaśī comes?
189-191 'Pārvatī, one who does not give up the vigil of Vāsudeva even  when depressed is most dear to me. Then again, I have no need  for one who is of a healthy mind and who stays at home but  does not perform the vigil of Hari. If a devotee of mine, deluded by sin, does not perform the vigil of Hari, then his worship is useless. He does not really worship me.
192 'Dancing on the night of the vigil of Visnu liberates a body  clad internally and externally with ten million sins.

Gaurī, those who give away lamps on the vigil of  Keśava will be rid of darkness and proceed to the highest  abode of Visnu.

If a man by his own will sings or dances with devotion  on the vigil of Padmanābha, what more is there for him to do?

CONSIDERING DVADAŚI  IN BREAKING THE FAST
It is said in the Padma Purāna:`When men transgress Dvādaśī 238  ít becomes very detrimental. It will remove dharma, as when
one does not bathe in the Sarasvatī:
DDT:'Transgresś means when one does not break the  fast within it. As when one does not bathe in the  Sarasvati' has the following meaning: when bathing at the  confluence of the Gańgā, Yamunā and Sarasvatī, one  should cross over the Gańgā and Yamunā and bathe on  the other side, since one should according to the rules  first bathe in Sarasvatī and then in the others. One who  does not follow this rule transgresses Sarasvatī and she  will thus take away that personś dharma.
In the Skanda Purāna:'One who transgresses Dvādaśī when 239-241  the day of breaking the fast has arrived and eats on Trayodaśī,
will take one hundred births in hell.' In the same book, in a  conversation between Mārkāndeya and Bhāgiratha (2.5.6.41):  `The devotee who does not complete the Dvādaśī throws his  earlier merit into the fire because of this: In the Kūrma Purāna: `One should fast on Ekādaśī and break the fast on Dvādaśī. One should not do that on Trayodaśī, since it would destroy the merit of twelve Dvādaśīs:
Furthermore:'One should not overstep Dvādaśī even by two 242-245  or three moments, for when overstepped, Dvādaśī will take away
onés earlier merit: In the Bhavisya Purāna:`Whatever done during twelve years is certainly immediately destroyed for the man  who breaks his fast after Dvādaśī: In the Devī-rahasya:'If one  oversteps Dvādaśī and then breaks the fast, then one's bathing  and so forth will all become fruitless. If Dvādaśī is short one  should perform one's mandatory duties at sunrise, or if very  short, after midnight but before midday.'

BREAKING THE FAST IF
THERE IS VERY LITTLE TIME  25o-251 In the Skanda Purāna:`On the order of Sambhu, if one notices  that the Dvādaśī lasts even half a moment after midnight, one  should quickly perform all his duties up to midday. If the Dvādaśī is so short that one does not have time to break the fast,  one should drink water. This is considered both eating and  not-eating by the wise:
DDT: Since drinking water is not considered eating by  the wise, one can eat later and avoid the fault of eating  twice. Also, since it is considered eating, one avoids the  fault of transgressing the Dvādaśī.
252-256 Furthermore:`If one notices that the Dvādaśī will last only two  or three moments after sunrise, one should perform duties such  as bathing and worship during the night: In the Kālikā- and  Sārada Purānas:`O king, when Dvādaśī is very short one should  perform duties such as bathing, giving in charity and performing sacrifices at night. How is one to break the fast if there is  very little time? By water, then there will be no fault of eating
twice: Kātyāyana says:`One performing a vrata without eating  should chant a mantra to Hari and then break the fast with  water if there is a risk for the proper time to pass: And also:  `Sandhya and such things are mandatory duties, breaking the  fast occasional. One should break the fast with water and then  perform sandhya, etc:

MANDATORINESS OF MAHA-DVADAŚI
282-283 In the Brahma-vaivarta Purāna: 'These eight Dvādaśīs have  been described by those learned in the Purānas. If one of them  is transgressed, they will destroy all one's merit: In the Padmaand Mārkāndeya Purānas the blessed Lord says: `Those who  do not perform the eight Dvādaśīs in this world will stay in  Yamaś abode until the end of the universe:
284-285 In the Skanda Purāna, in a conversation between Brahmā  and Nārada, in connection with the vigil: `One who neglects  Unmīlanī, Vañjulī or Paksavardhinī will stay in hell until fourteen Indras have passed. One who on earth does not perform  Trisprśā, dear to Visnu, will dwell in Yama's abode until the rivers have flowed into the oceans:
DDT: By connection with Unmīlanī and the others  mentioned in the Skanda Purāna, the quartet of Jayā and  so forth is also shown to be mandatory. Or then, within  these eight the four beginning with Unmīlanī are shown  since they are predominating. They are indeed manda(286-292) tory. This is the conclusion.
UNMĪLANI-VRATA  The following is from the Padma Purāna.`Śrī Sūta said: In days 293-294  of yore Ambarīsa ruled the earth. Once the great seer Gautama,
best of all ascetics, arrived in his court. Seeing him, the king got  up from his throne, offered him gifts and made him sit on the  trone. With great devotion he then spoke to him.
`Srī Ambarīsa said:"Welcome, tiger amongst sages! Please 295-296  be merciful! Now that you have come to my house I am most
fortunate. Is your penance going well nowadays? Is your devotion to Srī Keśava steady, not slipping out of your heart, o tiger  amongst sages?"
`Srī Gautama replied: "My practice is going well, o king, 297-3oI  and my devotion to Krsna is most steady. Best of kings, you al
ways protect the brāhmanas. Are you well? O lord of men,  what kind of devotional service to the Lord are you engaged  in? Do you daily see the Lord as a Sālagrāma? Do you always  praise the water that has bathed the Śālagrāma stone? Do you  daily take some of the bathing-water and drink it? Do you give  some to the Vaisnavas and then sprinkle the house with the  rest? Do you smear your limbs with the remains of the oil that  has been rubbed on the Śālagrāma? Do you every day touch a  garland of Sālagrāma-stones to your head and then wear it  around your neck with great devotion?
"'O lord of the earth, do you honour the remains of Krsnaś 302-304  incense with devotion? O king, do you perform ārātrika to
Visnu and then pray with devotion? Do you devotedly carry  the conch-water offered to Hari on your head? Do you always  touch offered items to your head and then give them to the  Vaisnavas? Do you present the food - with all kinds of ingredients - which the Lord of lords has tasted to Visvaksena and  then enjoy it together with the Vaisnavas?
"'Do you always devotedly praise Janārdana with the 305-309  Thousand Names? Do you offer the Lord valuable incense and
sing and dance? Do you adore Madhusūdana with durva-grass  at the beginning of worship? O tiger amongst men, do you
offer aksata to Keśava? Best of men, do you every fortnight perform the Dvādaśī-vrata that is pure together with the vigil? Do  you constantly worship Hari with great amounts of tulasī  leaves? Do you wear tilaka made of gopīcandana on your body?  Do you at all times carry a garland made of myrobalan fruits  around your neck, and a garland made of tulasī leaves, equal to  ten thousand sacrifices?
310-311 "`O king, do you always worship the Sālagrāma stone together with one from Dvāraka, one that bestows pleasure and  liberation? Lord of the earth, do you recite the Bhāgavata Purāna in front of Hari, and the story of Prahlāda and the king of  demons?
312-314 "`Master of the earth, do you seeing through the eyes of  scripture always diligently restrain men from performing a  mixed day of Vāsudeva? In a land where mixed days of Visnu  are being performed, the king is attacked by sin and becomes  eligible for hell. One should give up the four types of mixed  days of Hari and celebrate the pure ones. They will liberate ten  million relatives from hell and lead them to heaven:'
315-317 Ambarīsa said: "Best of brāhmanas, everything that you  have mentioned I do. I see this whole world, moving and nonmoving beings, as consisting of Visnu. Best of seers, you, the  embodied Visnu, have now come to my home. Please describe  to me, o brāhmana, a Vaisnava vrata that fulfills all desires. O  best of seers, one which, when performed, leaves nothing else  to be done, and which ensures that one will never return from  the world of Visnu!"'
318-32o And then (6.35.29-68): `Srī Gautama said: "Hear, lord of  the earth! I will describe a great Vaisnava vrata to you. The  merit that is born from this Dvādaśī I have not told anyone. O  great king, you are a Vaisnava. Hear with devotion the Vaisnava vrata which is most secret amongst men devoted to the  Lord. It is called Unmīlanī. Previously Visnu, being pleased,  mercifully explained it to me. Now, king, I will pass it on to you.
321-329 "`When a pure Ekādaśī lasts beyond sunrise the next day,  that second day is called Unmīlanī. It certainly destroys heaps
of sin. Whatever merit is connected with all holy places and  sanctuaries in the three worlds, sacrifices, Vedas and austerities is not equal to even a minute fraction of it. I have neither  heard of nor seen anything equal to Unmīlanī. Prayāga is not  equal to it, nor Kuruksetra, Kāśī, Mathurā, Puskara; rivers  Revā, Sarasvatī and Kalindī; the fields of Pindāraka, Prabhāsa,  Harakeśvara; the mountains of Himālaya, Meru, Gandhamādana, Malaya, Vindhya, Naisadha; rivers Godavari, Kaverī,  Candrabhāgā, Devikā, Tāpī, Payosnī, Siprā, Candanā, Carmanvatī, Sarayū, Gandakī, Gomati, Vipāśā nor the great Sona. O  king, what is the use of more words? There is no God higher  than Keśava, and nothing equal to Unmīlanī. All the sins of  those who observe Unmīlanī and worship Keśava are thrown  into the fire.
"`Lord of the earth, according to the rules one should wor- 330  ship Govinda with the name of the month in which the Unmīlanī tithi falls.
DDT: After describing its greatness he now speaks about  the worship from this verse up to verse 351.`The name of  the month': The twelve months, beginning with Mārga,  have names of Visnu connected with them, beginning  with Keśava and ending with Dāmodara. The corresponding name should be used, and also the form with its  respective placement of weapons.
"`One should fashion a golden form of Mādhava with the 331  name of the month and then worship Viśvarūpa with faith
and devotion according to one's means.
DDT: `Viśvarūpa' means He whose form is entirely  lovely, or then it means that one should worship the Lord  together with his limbs and weapons.
"`One should also establish a kumbha: a pot decorated with san- 332-334  dalwood paste, flowers and aksata and a tie of a garland, with
pure water and a little gold, a diamond, a sapphire, a ruby and a  pearl inside. On top of it a copper vessel filled with wheat or rice  should be placed. Govinda should be established on this kum
bha, and be bathed together with saffron, aloe and sandalwood.  Then one should smear Visnu with fragrant oil.
DDT: The idea is that one should establish a kumbha and  then.bathe the Lord upon it with milk, yoghurt, ghee, honey, sugarwater, and so on. The mantra for installation is:
ehy ehi tva¥ jagannātha vaikuntha purusottama  parivāraganopeta laksmyā saha jagatpate
`Come, come, Master of the universe, o Penetrating one,  Supreme person, together with your associates and with  Laksmi, o Lord of the world!'
The Lord should be called with this and then installed  with the mantra beginning with 'mano jūtir'. One should  offer sandalwood, flowers and so on with a mantra consisting of the particular name of the Visnu being worshipped.
335-338 "`O seer amongst kings, one should then offer two garments, a  sacred thread and an upper garment, shoes and a canopy above  the head. Having offered Mādhava a couch with all utensils, Vaisnavas should with great devotion worship the worshipable one  with incense, lamps, food, fruits, leaves, tulasī leaves and seasonal flowers.
339-34I "'The following mantras should be used: The name of the  month for the feet, Viśvarūpine namah (obeisance to Him who  embodies all) for the knees, Kāmapataye (Lord of love) for the  private parts, Pītavāsase (Who wears yellow clothes) for the hip,  Brahmā-mūrti-bhrte (Who takes the form of Brahmā) for the  navel, Viśvayonaye (Origin of the world) for the belly, Jñānagamyāya (Attainable by wisdom) for the heart, Vaikuntha-mūrtaye  ( Whose form pervades all) for the neck, Urugāyāya ( Widestrider) for the brow, Ksatrānta-kārine (Destroyer of the ksatriyas) for the arms, Sureśāya (Lord of the gods) for the upper  limbs and Sarvamūrtaye (The form of all) for all the limbs. The  honourable weapons should with devotion be worshipped with  their own names.
DDT: Here worship of all the limbs is described. All the  names should be followed by namah (obeisance to). With  these mantras one should worship the respective places.

`By hymns, offering lamps, songs and dance one should fully 348-352  please Hari, and by gifts of cloth, cows and food one should

The rest of the day should be spent for instance by  listening to stories about the Lord. 353-355 And also: `One who performs this Unmīlanī-vrata becomes  rich, lives long, gets sons and wisdom. The performer will not go  to hell.' The great seers declare that the gift  given away or the offering offered on Unmīlanī will be eternal:  VAÑJULI-VRATA
356-358 In the Padma Purāna, in a conversation between Gautama and  Ambarīsa:`Vañjulī, dear to Hari, is when Ekādaśī is pure and  Dvādaśī also, and Dvādaśī furthermore continues into Trayodaśī. Whether Vañjulī falls in the light or the dark fortnight,  one should eat on Ekādaśī and perform the vrata on Dvādaśī.  One should break the fast in the middle of the second day of  Dvādaśī, and not on Trayodaśī. O king, one who does this attains the fruit of ten thousand sacrifices.
THE MANTRA OF DECLARATION  359 dvādaśyān tu nirāhārah pāranā cāpare 'hani  dharmārtha-kāma-moksārtha¥ karisye vañjulī-vratam
"For the sake of piety, wealth, enjoyment and liberation I will perform the Vañjulī-vrata by not eating on Dvādaśī and by breaking  the fast on the next day:'
'One should bathe in a river, tank, lake or at home and then 360-363  perform one's daily duties. Having fashioned a form of Nārā
yana out of a small amount of gold one should put it in a bejewelled jar and on top a vessel of copper. One should according to  oneś means offer a canopy, a peacock-feather or a flute, shoes  and a pot of brass with ghee. The copper vessel should be filled  with wheat, and the Lord should be bathed and offered nyāsa.  One should smear Him with oil, and then the kumbha should  be covered with two cloths.
`The kumbha should be tied with a flower-garland and 364.-367  then the Lord inside should be worshipped. The Lord should
then be offered beautiful, fragrant flowers. The weapons should be worshipped with their respective names. Thus  God should be worshipped.

"`O Nārāyana! Lord of the universe! You who wear yellow garments! Janārdana! O great Visnu! O eternal one! Please lift me  up from the ocean of hell!

372 vrata¥ sampūrnatām yātu vañjulī-sambhava¥ mama  daśamī-samyutam deva yat krta¥ dvādasi-vratam  ajñānād athavā jñānāt paripūrna¥ tat astu me
"`Lord, lead my Vañjulī-vrata to completion. If this Dvādaśīvrata that I have performed has been connected with Daśamī  either unknowingly or knowingly, let it still be complete:'
373-377 `One who thus nicely offers arghya to the bane of Madhu  will stay in the splendid world of Visnu for a thousand kalpas.  Higher than a thousand Agnistoma-sacrifices is the Aśvamedha, and higher than a thousand Aśvamedhas is the Vājapeya.  Higher than a thousand Vājapeyas is the Pundarīka-sacrifice,  and higher than a thousand Pundarīkas is the Sautramani.  Higher than a thousand Sautramanis is the Rājasūya-sacrifice,  and higher than that, o king, is Vañjulī. Men who call out"Vañjulī!" in the age of Kali destroy sin from ten thousand births!
378-38o After worship, offering arghya and giving donations one  should offer incense, food and lamps to Visnu and then fully  honour the guru. One should give him cows, land, grain and  money. One should do this honestly in order to complete the  vrata. When the guru is pleased, Visnu is pleased, not otherwise. Therefore, one should worship the guru to please the  Carrier of the disk.
381-385 At night, one should keep vigil and listen to narrations  about Visnu. One should enthusiastically recite the Gītā, the  Thousand Names of Visnu and the Purāna spoken by Śuka in  order to please Hari. Anyone who recites or hears recieves the
fruit of donating a thousand cows for each book! One should  also sing, dance and play music in front of Hari. At sunrise, the  God and everything else should be given to the guru and one  should ask the Lord of gods and especially the guru for forgiveness. After performing all the occasional duties one should  eat together with friends:
In the Skanda Purāna, in a conversation between Brahmā 386-389  and Nārada, in connection with the vigil`The sin of forbidden
sexual relationships or eating what one should not eat, is destroyed on the day of Vañjulī. The sin of stealing land, or stealing  from God; the sin of cheating with jewels or scales; of stealing  gold; sin done unknowingly or knowingly; in an earlier birth  or in this birth: all is removed by performing a single day of  Vañjulī. One will have no mental suffering and no illnesses  causing excessive suffering.'
In the Brahma-vaivarta Purāna, in a conversation between 390  Sūta and Saunaka: `O twice-born one, on the day of Vañjulī
He who rides on Garuda leaves His abode, goes to earth and  makes His dwelling there.
DDT: `There means amongst those who perform the  Vañjulī-vrata. In another reading it says that he 'gives  wealth', meaning that He gives what people want or that  He fulfills the desires of those who desire riches.
`When Yama, son of the Sun, sees a brāhmana averse to Vañ- 39I-393  julī he excitedly makes an agreement with Citragupta. "This
fool, averse to the vratas of Visnu will come to my abode. Remove all good deeds he has already performed! This person is  nothing but a headache for me, he always torments me:"
Furthermore: `Vañjulī is equal to the best of all vratas, the 394-399  king of all holy places, the gift of all gifts. A person who at that
time gives food to the twice-born with faith will attain the  abode of Krsna even if he is a sinner. One who at that time  worships Laksmī and Nārāyana made of gold and gives donations of food according to his means will attain Vaikuntha. O  brāhmana, if men who have fallen from their duties through
lust, greed or stupidity perform Vañjulī, they will be rid of three  generations of sin. Indeed, to fast on Vañjulī is the goal of all  scriptures, the opinion of all learned men, established by all  righteous men. A man who performs Vañjulī by fasting and by  honouring the brāhmanas according to his means will indeed  go to the highest abode:
TRISPRŚA-VRATA  400-401 In the Brahma-vaivarta Purāna:'When the Madhusūdanī Dvādaśī falls on the bright fortnight of the month of Vaiśākha it is  known as Trisprśā, and it destroys ten millions of sins. If this  Madhusūdanī Dvādaśī in Vaiśākha moreover falls on a Wednesday, it will fulfill all the desires of men:
4o2-404 In the same book, Dvārakā-māhātmya:'If Ekādaśī is in the  beginning, Dvādaśī in the middle and Trayodaśī at the end of  the same day, one should fast, worship and sing in a temple of  Krsna on that rare occasion. By a single such fast one attains  the fruit of ten thousand sacrifices. In the age of Kali, during  this day the vigil at home is a hundred thousand times and the  dancing ten million times more effective, what to speak of doing these things in a temple of Krsna:
405-408 In the Padma Purāna, in a conversation between Sanat-kumāra and Vyāsa (6.34.2-77):"Now listen with attention! I will  tell you about the great Trisprśā-vrata, which eradicates all  offences and sins. The vrata for Visnu called Trisprśā bestows  pleasure to materialists and liberation to the desireless. Listen  to my narration! Great sage, if someone in the age of Kali always glorifies Trisprśā, Keśava is personally honoured by him.  Stern preparatory rites cannot take away all sins, but simply  mentioning"Trisprśá' can doubtlessly do that.
409-411 `The Agamas, Purānas, all the holy places, performing many  vratas or worshipping the gods cannot lead to liberation if one  has not performed Trisprśā. For the sake of liberation the God  of gods has created this queen of tithis. O brāhmana, to those  controlled by their senses, who have no understanding of medi
tation or the object of meditation, who are addicted to enjoying  lusty desires, Trisprśā immediately awards liberation.
'Previously, I was present when Visnu, carrier of the Cakra, 412-414  explained this to Śańkara, four-faced Brahmā and others on
the banks of the ocean of milk: "I give liberation to those who  perform Trisprśā, even if they do not control their senses or  know no Sańkhya-philosophy." Therefore, best of sages, perform Trisprśā, giver of liberation, in the company of saints!  Great sage, give up Sańkhya!
'If Trisprśā falls in the light fortnight of Kārttika and on a 415-420  Wednesday it destroys ten million sins. O seer, on this day  Maheśvara fasted and was freed from the sin of murder. By
fasting on Trisprśā at the advice of Bhrgu, the scull of the  brāhmana immediately fell from his hand. O great sage, by  fully fasting on Trisprśā eight generations of powerful forefathers got rid of the sin of killing thousands of brāhmanas.  Through the advice of Mādhava, goddess Gańgā became liberated from the sins of Kali by fully fasting on Trisprśā. By not  eating on Trisprśā the sin of killing thousands of brāhmanas is  destroyed, what to speak of lesser evils.
`O best of brāhmanas, liberation does not appear in Pra- 421-423  yāga, Kāśī, Gomatī or a temple of Krsna, but through fasting
on Trisprśā. Only by dying in Prayāga or Kāśī, and only by bathing in Gomatī does one attain liberation, not otherwise, but by  fasting on Trisprśā one attains liberation even at home. Through  Sańkhya-philosophy it is very difficult to achieve liberation for  someone who has uncontrolled senses and who is attached to  lusty desires. Therefore, o best of the brāhmanas, perform Trisprśā, giver of liberation!
'Śrī Vedavyāsa said: "What is this Trisprśā-dvādaśī like, 0 424  best of sages? Please now tell more about this liberator of men!"
'Srī Sanatkumara replied:"O brāhmana, Mādhava once spo- 425  ke about Trisprśā, giver of great boons, on the banks of the
Prācī Sarasvatī, in front of Jāhnavī Gańgā:'
`Srī Jāhnavī said: "In the age of Kali, people carrying the 426-427  burdens of enormous sins such as those of killing brāhmanas,
bathe in my waters, and by these hundreds of sins my body is  burned and defiled. O Lord, You who ride on Garuda, how shall  I be freed from these sins?"
428-43I `Srī Prācī Mādhava said: "Without a doubt I will instruct  you, child. Do not cry! Before me is my abode, Srīsthala. O  best of goddesses, there in front of me flows Prācīdevī, Sarasvatī. If you bathe there you will become magically cleansed.  Where Prācī Sarasvatī is, without a doubt there I also reside  together with hundreds of millions of holy places and gods.  Where Prācī Sarasvatī is, all sins are destroyed, especially in  front of me, and especially in the age of Kali:'
432 `Srī Jāhnavī said:"Lord of gods, I am not able to always go  there. O Mādhava, please tell me how I can get rid of sin here!"  433-435 `Srī Prācī Mādhava answered: "Higher than the Sarasvatī,
millions of holy places, millions of sacrifices, gifts, vratas, austerities, muttering mantras, Sañkhya or Yoga is Trisprśā, awarder of  the fruit of the four stages of life. Celebrate this vrata, beautiful  one! O best of rivers, in whatever month it falls, whether in the  light or dark forthnight, you should perform it. It will take away  your sin:'
436-437 `Śrī Mandākinī said:"O Mādhava, please tell me what this  Trisprśā is. Tell me today also about its greatness. When Daśamī, Ekādaśī and Dvādaśī all occur on the same day, that is  called Trisprśā. Lord, is it like this? O master, I do not know, so  please tell me:'
438-44I `Śrī Prācī Mādhava replied: "O goddess, the Trisprśā you  have described is demoniac! It should be diligently avoided,  like a sannyāsi without vows. It gives life and strenght to the  demons and devils. It should be carefully avoided, like a menstruating woman. Just like one always avoids contact with a  woman in her monthly courses, so Vaisnavas should avoid my  day if it has been touched by Daśamī. O Jāhnavī, one who has  my grace gets hundreds of thousands of sins destroyed, but  those who are without it, Trisprśā will lead into misfortune.
442-446 "`When Ekādaśī, Dvādaśī and at the end of night Trayodaśī are combined, that is known as Trisprśā, not when Daśa
mī is involved. One who performs a vrata when Ekādaśī is  combined with Daśamī drinks poison and eats the excrement  of dogs. Knowing this, never celebrate my day when it is combined with Daśamī, for it will destroy all the merit of millions  of lives. If there is doubt, especially if the fortnight is lenghtened,  then on my order one should always perform my dear Dvādaśī. Those devoted to me should on my order celebrate my  day and know how to make sure that it is not contaminated by  Daśamī:'
`Śrī Vedavyasa said:"O brāhmana, tell me about the rules I 447  am to follow!"
`Śrī Sanatkumāra replied: "One should according to one's 448-450  means fashion a form of Dāmodara of gold. One should take a

One  should perform nyāsa, bathe the Lord and smear Him with oil.  Then one should devotedly cover each jar with a cloth.

462-466 "`Then one should offer ārātrika with incense, lights and  foods. After having worshipped the Lord of the god of gods one should  perform the vigil of Hari by singing, dancing and reading the  scriptures. At the end of night one should again properly offer  arghya to the Lord. After performing duties such as bathing  one should eat together with brāhmanas:"
PAKSAVARDHINI-VRATA  467-472 In the Padma Purāna it is stated by Brahmā (6.36.2, 4-22): `If  the New Moon or Full Moon tithi is full, that is longer than 24  hours, and continues into the next day, then the preceding Dvādaśī is Paksavardhinī, equal to thousands of Aśvamedhas. O
best of the brāhmanas, now listen to the rules for its worship!  After fully worshipping Visnu with mantras, one should please  Him by an offering of arghya. One should install a new kumbha, filled with water and smeared with sandalwood, with some  gold, a diamond, a sapphire, a ruby and a pearl inside and tied  with a flower garland, and upon it a vessel of copper filled with  rice. One should fashion a form of Mādhava out of gold, and  then bathe this God with milk, yoghurt, ghee, honey and sugarwater. Then one should smear Him with saffron, aloe and sandalwood. One should offer a pair of cloths, a parasol and shoes.
`Now one should worship the Lord of gods, situated on the 473-476  kumbha, with Padmanābhaya for the feet, Yogamūrtaye for the
knees, Nrsi¥hāya for the thighs, Jñānapradāya (Giver of knowledge) for the hip, Viśvanāthāya (Lord of all) for the belly,  Srīdharāya (Abode of the goddess of fortune) for heart, Kaustubha-kanthāya (Whose neck is adorned with the Kaustubhajewel) for the neck, Ksatrāntakāya for the arms, Vyomamūrtāya (Whose form is space) for the brows, Sarvarūpine for the  head, their own names for the weapons and Divyarūpine namah  (Obeisance to Him whose form is divine) for all the limbs.  Having worshipped according to the rules one should then offer  arghya with a beautiful coconut to the God of gods, carrying  the disk. This mantra should be used:
saritsārārnava-potāya pāpakaksā-mahānala 477  narakāgni praśamana janma-mrtyu jarāpaha
mā¥ uddhara jagannātha patita¥ bhava-sāgare 478  grhānārghya¥ mayā datta¥ padmanābha namo śtu te
"'O boat on the ocean of repeated birth and death, great fire for  heaps of sin, extinguisher of the fires of hell, remover of birth,  death and old age, o Lord of the universe, please save me! I  have fallen into the ocean of worldly existence. Accept this argya that I offer. Obeisances to You, lotus-naveled one:'
`One should then offer attractive, tasty and juicy fruits to 479-484  Mādhava and also incense with aloe, camphor, ghee and bdel
lium with devotion to the Lord. Also, a lamp with ghee or sesame-seed oil should be offered. When one has done all this according to the rules, worship of the guru should be performed. One should give the guru clothes, a turban, a jacket and money according to one's means. One should offer him food and betel and then fully please him by giving him the offered arghya. Then one should pass the day engaged in one's own business or as one is able, if poor, and then perform the vigil with song and dance:
JAYA-VRATA 485-486 In the Brahmā Purāna, in a conversation between Vaśistha and Mandhātr: `If the moon is in the asterism Punarvasu on a Dvādaśī in the light forthnight, that Dvādaśī is known by the name Jayā, and it is the foremost of tithis. A person who fasts on that day will not fall into terrible hell, but without a doubt attain a fruit equal to that from sacrifices such as the Agnistoma:
487 jayā-vratam anustheyam yathaivonmīlanī-vratam
The Jayā-vrata should be celebrated just like the Unmīlanī-vrata. 488 As it is said by Mārkāndeya: `One should perform the Jayāvrata in a place where the water that has bathed a Śālagrāma and that which is mixed with tulasī is present:
DDT: The Jayā-vrata should be performed at places such as the confluences of rivers.
VIJAYA-VRATA 489-492 In the same place in the Brahmā Purāna:`When the asterism Sravana is present during Dvādaśī in the light fortnight, that tithi is called Vijayā, and it is the very best of tithis: In the Visnu-dharmottara: `When the asterism Sravana is present during Dvādaśī in the light fortnight, that most meritorious Dvādaśī is known as Vijayā. For men, bathing at that time is like bathing at all holy places, and having worshipped at that
time, one attains the fruit of a whole year's worship. By chanting one mantra one attains the fruit of chanting a thousand times. The merit of giving gifts is thousandfold, so also feeding the brāhmanas, sacrifices and fasting.'

JAYANTI-VRATA In the Brahmā Purāna: `When the constellation Rohinī ap- 506-509 pears on a Dvādaśī in the light fortnight, that tithi is known by
