THE PRAYER MANTRA
55I jāmadagnya namas te śtu ksatriyānta-karāya ca  sarvāni yāni pāpāni sapta janma-krtāny api
552 ksaya¥ yāntu mamaivādya tvat-prasādāc ca bhārgava  vācika¥ mānasa¥ pāpa¥ jñānato jñānato 'pi vā
`O son of Jamadagni, obeisances to You, destroyer of the ksatriyas! Today, through Your mercy, descendant of Bhrgu, destroy all my sin, even that committed during seven births, by  words, in the mind, knowingly or unknowingly!
553 āyur yaśas tathārogya¥ dhana¥ dhānyañ ca sampadam  saubhāgya¥ lava bhaktasya santāna¥ vipula¥ bhavet
`May Your devotee always have an abundance of longevity, beauty,  good health, wealth, grain, success, fortune and descendants.  554 sarvān kāmān āpnuvāni divya¥ saukhya¥ nirantaram
ante py astu mameśāna bhaktis tvac-carane prabho  Attaining all desires and endless divine bliss, o Lord, may I even  at the end have devotion to Your feet, o Master.
555 janārdana hrsīkeśa laksmīnātha surārcita  rāma rāma mahābāho kārtavīrya-vināśana
556 etat sarva¥ mayā datta¥ jñāna¥ jñeya¥ tavācyuta  mām uddhara jagannātha daya¥ krtvā mamopari
`O Janārdana, Hrsīkeśa, Lord of Laksmī, worshipped by the gods,  Rāma, Rāma, strong-armed one, killer of the son of Kartavīrya!  All this I offer You. O Acyuta, You are knowledge and the object of  knowledge. Lord of the universe, save me! Have mercy upon me!'
WORSHIP OF THE MYROBALAN TREE
pītā pītāmahāś cānye aputrā ye ca gotrinah 557  vrksa yoni¥ gatā ye ca ye ca kītatvam āgatah
raurave narake ye ca mahā-raurava-sarñjñake 55g  viyoni¥ ca gatā ye ca ye ca brahmānda-madhya gāh
piśācatva¥ gatā ye ca ye ca pretatvam āgatah 559  te pibantu mayā datta¥ dhātrī-mūle sadā payah
te sarve trptim āyāntu dhātrī-mūla-nisecanāt 560
A father, grandfather or any relative who has no son, who has  been born as a tree, become a worm, gone to the hell Raurava  or to the one known as Mahā-raurava, who has taken a low  birth, entered the middle of the universe, become a witch or a  ghost: may they all always drink the water I have poured at the  root of this myrobalan tree. May they all become nourished by  my sprinkling of water at the root of the myrobalan:
iti dhātrī¥ cāhhisicya vārān astottara¥ śatam 56r  tāñ ca pradaksinīkrtya kuryāj jāgarana¥ vratī
After saying this, the performer of the vrata should sprinkle  water one hundred and eight times and then circumambulate  the tree. Then he should perform the vigil.
prātaś ca deva¥ nīrājya nitya¥ karma samāpya ca 562  mūrtyādi gurave dattvā prāgvat pāranam ācaret
In the morning one should perform ārātrika and then one's  daily duties. After giving the form, etc, to the guru one should,  as before, break the fast.
phālgune māsi yady esā dvādaśi pāpanāśinī 563  bhavet tadā vratasyāsya mahimā syād viśesatah
If the Pāpanāśinī Dvādaśī comes in the month of Phālguna,  then the glory of this vrata becomes especially great.
CONCLUSION  564 iti kramena likhita¥ vijayādi-vrata-trayam
bhavisyottara-skāndābhyām śrībrahmānda purānatah
Thus the three vratas beginning with Vijayā have been described according to the Bhavisya-, Skanda- and Srī Brahmānda Purānas.
DDT: For shortnesses sake the three vratas beginning  with Vijayā and their rules have been described according  to the Uttara-khanda of the Bhavisya and other Purānas,  but not by directly quoting their statements, fearing to  expand the book too much. Therefore the Bhavisya, etc,  have not been mentioned while describing the rules. The  Vijayā-vrata follows the Uttara-khanda of the Bhavisya  Purāna (4.76) the Jayantī-vrata the Skanda Purāna, and  the Pāpanāśinī-vrata the Brahmānda Purāna.
565 anye pi dvādasi-bhedā bahavah santi viśrutāh  agrato lekhanīyās te tat-tan-māsa-prasañgatah
There are also many other kinds of famous Dvādaśīs. They will  be described further on in connection with the respective month  in which they occur.
Thus ends the thirteenthVilāsa, called `Celebrating the Visnu-vrata',  in the Śrī Bhagavad-bhakti-vilāsa, written by Śrī Gopāla Bhatta.




FROM VILĀSA XIV  FESTIVALS OF THE
FIRST HALF OF THE YEAR  BHAIMI EKADAŚI
In the Matsya Purāna (69.Z,12-13): `Śrī Brahmā said: "O im- 174-175  mortal lord, how can men attain freedom from disease, endless
wealth and liberation by only a little austerity?" Srī Maheśvara  replied:"Your question is exemplary, Brahmā. The answer is a  great secret of religion, and it will be explained to Bhīma, the  wolfbelly, later on:"
Furthermore (69.16-18):'This vrata is foremost of all vratas. 176-178  Vāsudeva, the self of all, the teacher of the world, will explain it. It
bestows the fruit of all sacrifices, it destroys all sins, it kills all demons and it is honoured by all gods. It is the purest of the pure,  the bliss of all bliss, the last of the coming and the first of the gone:
DDT:'The last of the coming and the first of the gone'  means that this is the last amongst vratas to come, but  not only that, it is also first amongst those in the past. In  this way a special greatness is shown. In the same book  the Lord says to Bhīma: `Fully perform this vrata that I  have explained to you lovingly. Since you will perform  this vrata, o steadfast one, it will be named after you. This  Bhīma-dvādaśī, which previously was called Kalyāninī, is  auspicious. It takes away all sin:
In the same book, the Lord says to Bhīma (69.19-20):`O Bhā- 179-180  rata, when you are unable to fast on Astamī (the eight tithí),  Caturdaśī (the fourteenth tithi), Dvādaśī or any other day, then
this tithi is most auspicious. It removes sin. Fast according to  the rules and go to the highest abode of Visnu!'
Moreover, in the same book, at the end of the descriptions
of the rules (69.62):'Indra, the Vasus and the gods could not 181  describe the fruit one attains by performing this vrata, even if  they had a billion tongues!'
vrate krtya-vidhiś cāsmin pūjā-vidhi-viśesavān  vaisnavaiś ced apeksyah syāj jñeyo matsya purānatah
If Vaisnavas desire to perform this vrata, the rules for performing it and the particular rules for worship are found in the  Matsya Purāna.
DDT: There ís not a great need of such rules for Vaisnavas, since this vrata is not mandatory for them. The  rules are thus given ín the Matsya Purāna by the Lord to  Bhīma (69.21-55): 'On Daśamī during the bright fortnight of Māgha one should rub the body with ghee and  then bathe with sesame-seed oil. Then, one should worship Visnu with the mantra Namo Nārāyanāya, the feet  with Krsnāya, the head with Sarvātmane, the throat with  Vaikunthaya, the chest with Srīvatsadhārine, the arms  with Sañkhine (Carrier of the conch), Cakrine (Carrier  of the disk), Gadine (Carrier of the club), Varadāya (Giver  of blessings), one after another and all with Nārāyanāya,  the belly with Dāmodarāya, the penis with Pañcaśarāya  (Carrier of five arrows), the thighs with Saubhāgya-māthāya (Churner of success), the knees with Bhūtadhārine  (maintainer of living beings), the shank with Nīlāya (Dark  one) and the feet with Viśvasrje namah (Obeisance to the  creator of all).
'The goddess of fortune should be worshipped with  Namas Tustyai (Satisfaction), Pustyai (Nourishment),  Vrstyai (Rain) and Hrstyai (Ecstasy). Garuda should always be worshipped with Namo Vihaganāthāya (Lord of  birds), Vāyuvegāya (Fleet as the wind), Paksine (Bird)  and Visapramāthine (Destroyer of poison).
`In this way Govinda should be worshipped together  with Umāpati and Ganeśa, with sandalwood paste, incense and different kinds of foodstuffs. Then one should  silently eat krsarā (a preparation of rice, peas and sesame)  sprinkled with gavya and milk with ghee. Then the wise  person should recite his mantra, take hold of a tooth-twig  of banyan or khādira (Acacia Catechu) and clean his  teeth facing east. After performing his duties at dusk he  should utter the following when the sun has set:
namo nārāyanāyeti tvam aha¥ śarana¥ gatah  ekādaśyā¥ nirāhārah samabhyarcya ca keśavam  rātriñ ca sakalā¥ sthitvā snānañ ca payasā tathā  sarpisā cāpi dahana¥ hutvā brāhmana-puñgavail7  sahaiva pundarīkāksa dvādaśyā¥ ksīra-bhojanam  karisyāmi yatātmāha¥ nirvighnenāstu tac ca me
"'Obeisance to Nārāyana! I have taken my refuge in You.  Self-restrained I will fast on Ekādaśī, and after worshipping Keśava I will stay up all night. I will bathe You with  milk and sacrifice with ghee and fire. O Lotus-eyed Lord,  together with excellent brāhmanas I will eat sweet rice on  Dvādaśī. May I accomplish this without hindrance!"
After saying this one should sleep on the ground. In  the morning one should listen to stories from the Itihāsas  and then offer libations to the manes according to the  rules. After bowing to the faultless Hrsīkeśa and seeing  the sun, a thoughtful person should have a pavillion constructed in front of his house. O lord of peoples, it should  be ten hastas (elbow to the tip of the middle finger) or  eight karas (the breadth of 24 fingers) long. Destroyer of  demons, one should construct a beautiful verandah of  four hastas, with a doorway of the same breadth.
'One should fashion a waterpot with twelve holes in  the bottom and fill it with water. Sitting on the skin of a  black antelope, one should keep the stream of water from  it on oneś head during all night. One who understands  the Uedas knows that by the many streams a manyfold  fruit will come. Therefore, o best of the Kurus, this stream  should be carried to the best of onés ability. In the same  way, one should pour a stream of milk on the head of  Visnu.
'Then one should make a sacrificial arena one aratni  (elbow to the tip of the little finger) long in the form of a  conical triangle with three girdles around it. Like those  who keep only one fire, brāhmanas devoted to Visnu  should then with mantras offer grains, ghee, sesame and  caru (rice, barley and pulse boiled with butter and milk)  with ghee from cow's milk. A stream of ghee, the size of  half a basket, should then be dropped into the fire.
`Great hero, one should establish 13 kumbhas with five  jewels inside, with different kinds of foodstuffs, decorated with white cloths and with vessels made of copper  on top of them. Facing the north a homa should be performed by four hotrs, four priests muttering prayers to  Rudra and devoted to the Yajur-veda and by four Vaisnavas, expert in the Sāma-veda. Before and afterwards,  prayers to avert misfortune should be recited.
`Then, without duplicity, these twelve brāhmanas should  be honoured with cloth, garlands, ointments, rings, bracelets, golden strings, garments and beds. The preceptor  should receive twice the amount of everything. In the morning, one should gather 13 faultless, beautiful milking cows  with golden faces, silvery hooves and milkpails of brass together with their calves, all sprinkled with sandalwood  paste. These should also be donated, o best of the Kurus.
After this all the brāhmanas should be given nice refreshments and be fed with different kinds of eatables.  One should oneself give up food not containing ksāra or  salt. Then one should, together with son and wife, follow  them with eight steps and declare:
priyatām atra deveśa keśava kleśanāśana
"`Please be happy here, o Lord of gods, Keśava, destroyer  of suffering!"
`Having said this, the wise should send the kumbhas,  cows, beds and clothes to the houses of the brāhmanas. In  the absence of many beds, one nicely decorated bed  should be given to the guru. O best of men, one who desires wealth should spend that day listening to the Itihāsas  and Purānas.`
GOVINDA DVADAŚI  phalgune dvādaśī śuklā yā pusyarksena samyutā  govinda-dvādasi nāma sā syād govinda-bhaktidā
The Dvādaśī in the bright fortnight of Phalguna, combit  with the asterism Pusya, is called Govinda Dvādaśī, and it  stows devotion to Govinda.
tasyām uposya vidhinā bhagavanta¥ prapūjayet 223  likhitah pāpanāśinyā¥ vidhir yo 'trāpi sa smrtah
At that time one should fast and worship the Lord according  to the rules. The rules written in connection with Pāpanāśini  Mahā-dvādaśī apply here as well.
THE GREATNESS OF GOVINDA DVADAŚI
In the Brahma Purāna, in a conversation between Vaśistha 224-225  and Māndhātr:`If Dvādaśī in the bright fortnight of Phalguna
is combined with Pusya, it is called Govinda Dvādaśī, and it  destroys great sin. A man who fasts according to the rules at  that time has his sins destroyed and attains the highest perfection, from where there is no return.`
āmardakī dvādaśīti loke khyāteyam eva hi 226  yogābhāve'tra tan-nāmni tadīyaikādaśī matā
yatra āmardakī-pūjā- vratam asyā¥ viśesatah
This Dvādaśī is also known amongst people as Amardakī  Dvādaśī. If there is no connection with Pusya, then the corresponding Ekādaśī is known by that name. The speciality of  this day is the vrata of honouring the myrobalan tree.
DDT: If the Dvādaśī is combined with Pusya it is necessary to fast on that day. Otherwise one should fast on  Ekādaśī, and also at that time perform the rituals such as  honouring the myrobalan tree.
RULES FOR AMARDAKI-VRATA
As said by Brahmā in the same book, in connection with the
greatness of Pāpanāśinī:`O king, in the month of Phalguna es- 227-228  pecially the vrata of Amardakī is said to be great. It is auspi
cious and it awards men the abode of Visnu: In the Skanda Purāna, Prabhāsa-khanda, in a discussion between Devī and Ma
heśvara (7.2.17.199-205): `In the bright fortnight of Phalguna  one should fast on Ekādaśī. Having bathed in a river, in a pond  or with water from a well or in the house, one should go to a  mountain or a forest were a myrobalan tree grows.
229-230 `When a tree appeared from churning the ocean of milk, it  was called "Amardakī" because of the rough handling (āmarda) of the gods and demons. This tree is also known as Śivā  and Laksmī, and it is honoured by the best of gods. The gods  headed by Brahmā all know this tree to be connected with  Visnu.
231-234. , Arriving there, one should worship Hari or Śiva at the root  of the tree with pure flowers, and then keep vigil during the  night. One should install a pot full of water with a vessel on  top, offer food made from havisya and a lamp according to the  rules. In this way, those devoted to listening to stories perform  the vigil and, while embodied, are freed from the sins of Kali,  born from the body. At the end of this body, again, they are all  honoured in the temple of Hari:
DAMANAKAROPANA DVADAŚI  328 caitrasya śukla-dvādaśyā¥ damanāropanotsavam  vidadhyāt tad-vidhir baudhāyānādy-ukto'tra likhyate
On the Dvādaśī of the bright fortnight of Caitra one should perform the celebration of offering a damana plant (Artemisia  Indica). The rules are given here, following the writings of Baudhāyāna and others.
madhoh sitaikadaśyāñ ca prātah-krtya¥ samāpya ca  gatvā damanakārāmā¥ tatrāśoka¥ smara¥ yajet
329 On the Ekādaśī of the bright fortnight of Caitra, one should  after performing the morning duties, enter a damanaka garden  and there worship Smara, the god of love, as an aśoka tree  ( Jonesia Asoka).
THE MANTRA
aśokāya namas tubhya¥ kāma-strī-śoka-nāśanam 330  śokārti¥ hara me nityam ānanda¥ janayasva me
`Obeisance to the aśoka tree, to you, remover of the sorrow of  love and women. Please always take away the pain of my sorrow and give me happiness!'
DDT: In the damanaka garden one should worship Smara  in the form of an aśoka-tree with aksata, sandalwood pulp,  and so on. This worship should be understood to be indeed of the Lord in the form of the god of love. Or then  the offering to the Lord is just made in the same way as  one would worship the god of love.
nesyāmi krsna-pūjārtham tva¥ krsna-prīti-kārakam 331  iti samprārthya natvā ca grhnīyād damana¥ śubham
`I will take you away for worshipping Krsna, for you give love  for Krsna'. Praying like this, one should bow down and take a  beautiful damana.
DDT:`Také: if one does not have a damanaka garden of  oneś own, one may take a plant one from someone else's.  `Beautiful' means that it should have very wonderful blossoms.
proksya tat pañca gavyena praksālyādbhih prapūjya ca 332  vastrenāccādya vedādi- ghosenagrham ānayet
The plant should be sprinkled with the five substances of the  cow and water. It should then be worshipped and covered with  a cloth. With the sound of recitations from the Uedas, and so  on, it should be brought home.
RULES FOR PRELIMINARY  PURIFICATION OF THE DAMANAKA
333 krsnasyāgre samuddhrtya sarvatobhadra-mandalam  nidhāya damana¥ tatra rātrau tad adhivāsayet
In front of Krsna a Sarvatobhadra mandala should be drawn.  The damana plant should be placed there, and in the evening  preliminary purification should be done.
DDT: The plant should be placed in a basket in the  mandala. After the duties of the evening and special worship of the Lord, adhivāsana or preliminary purification  should be performed.
THE MANTRA
334 pūjārtha¥ deva-devasya visnor laksmī-pateh prabhoh  damana tvam ihāgaccha sānnidhya¥ kuru te namah
O damana, please come here for the worship of the God of gods,  Visnu, Husband of Laksmī, the Lord. Please appear! Obeisance  to you.
335 sabīja¥ kāmadevañ ca tathā bhasma-śarīrakam  anañga¥ manmathañ caiva vasanta-sakham eva ca  smaran tatheksucāpañ ca puspabānañ ca pujayet
336 prāg-ādi-diksu ratyādhya¥ vidhivad damane kramāt
With the seed-mantra one should according to the rules in the  eight directions around the damana plant, beginning in the  east, worship Kāmadeva (the god of love), Bhasma-śarīraka  (whose body is ashes), Anañga (the bodiless), Manmatha (agitater of the mind), Vasanta-sakha (the friend of spring), Smara  (love), Iksucāpa (whose eyebrows are like bows) and Puspabāna (whose arrows are flowers), together with Rati.
DDT: One by one these eight forms of the god of love  should be worshipped with the Kāma seed-mantra around  the Damanaka. According to the ruleś means with sugar,  aksata, sandalwood pulp, etc. An example: `klīm drūī¥  kāmadevāya namah, drūīm ratyai namah'. Alternatively  one may say as when performing rituals such as the Keśava-nyāsa:`klī¥ kāmadevāya ratyai namah'.
astottara-śata¥ kāma- gāyatryā cābhimantrya tat 337  dattvā puspāñjali¥ kāma- deva¥ vandeta mantravat
Then one should read 1o8 Kāma-gāyatrīs over the plant, and  after offering a handful of flowers worship the god of love with  the following mantra:
namo śtu puspa-bānāya jagad-āhlāda-kārine 338  manmathāya jagannetre rati prīti-pradāyine
`Obeisance to him who carries flower-arrows, who gives joy to  the world, who agitates the mind, who is the leader of the world  and who bestows passion and satisfaction.
āmantrito śi deveśa purāna-purusottama 339  atas tvā¥ pūjayisyāmi sānnidhya¥ kuru keśava
`I call you, Lord of gods, oldest and highest person! I am going  to worship You, so please arrive, o Keśava!
nivedayāmy aha¥ tubhya¥ prātar damanaka¥ śubham 340  sarvathā sarvadā visno namas te śtu prasīda me
`In the morning I will offer You a beautiful damanaka. O Visnu, in all circumstances and at all times I bow to You. Be merciful unto me!'
ittham āmantrya deveśa¥ dattvā puspāñjali¥ punah 341  gīta-nrtyādinā rātrau kuryāj jāgarana¥ mudā
After praising the Lord of gods and after again offering a handful of flowers, one should happily keep vigil at night with song,  dance, and so forth.
DDT: The vigil should be performed before the Lord  seated in His swing. If one is personally not able, then one  should perform it through ones son or someone else, in  the place of the purification of the damana.
RULES FOR OFFERING THE DAMANAKA  342 prātah-snānādi nirvartya nitya pūjā¥ vidhāya ca  damanaropanārthañ ca mahā pūjā¥ samācaret
After performing the morning duties such as bathing and the  mandatory worship, one should offer elaborate worship in connection with offering the damana plant.
343 tato damanaka¥ bhaktyā pānibhyā¥ parigrhya ca  ghantādi-vādyaghosena śrīkrsnāya samarpayet
One should then take hold of the damanaka with both hands,  and to the accompaniment of the sound of bells and other instruments offer it to Srī Krsna.
DDT: `Offer' means that one should first offer a damanaka blossom to the head of the Lord, and then in a tasteful way to the blessed feet, and so on.
MANTRA FOR OFFERING THE DAMANAKA  344 deva-deva jagannātha vāñcbitārtba-pradāyaka
krtsnān pūraya me krsna kāmān kāmeśvarī-priya
`God of gods, master of the universe, giver of desired things, o  Krsna, o You who are dear to the goddess of love, please entirely  fulfill my desires!
DDT: `The goddess of love' means Rati. Krsna is called  dear to her as He is worshipped as the god of love. Alternatively, it refers to the giver of all love, goddess Laksmī,  or then to the fulfiller of all of Krsna's desires, Śrī Rādhā.
ida¥ damanaka¥ deva grhāna mad-anugrahāt 345  imā¥ sā¥vatsarī¥ pūjā¥ bhagavann iha pūraya
`Please accept this damanaka, Master, to favour me. O Lord,  please complete the worship of the year!'
tato dāmanakī¥ mālā¥ gandhādīni samarpya ca 346  gītādinotsava¥ krtvā śrī-krsna¥ prārthayed idam
Then one should offer a damanaka garland, sandelwood pulp  and so on. After a celebration with song, etc, one should pray  like this to Srī Krsna:
DDT: A damanaka garland' means a garland made of  damanaka blossoms. After offering it, one should offer  the five articles: sandelwood pulp, flowers, incense, lamps  and eatables. Then one should hold a celebration with  song, dance, etc, in honour of the festival of offering the  damanaka, and then pray.
mani-vidruma-mālābhir mandāra-kusumādibhih 347  iya¥ samvatsarī pūjā tavāstu garuda-dhvaja
`Together with garlands of pearls and coral, and flowers such  as those of the coral tree (Erythina Indica), this is the worship  of the year. May it be Yours, rider of Garuda!
DDT:`May this worship that I have done by offeringYou  a damanaka be like offering a garland of pearls and coral,  etc. Just as those things are dear to You, be pleased with  this also: This is the implied meaning.
vanamālā¥ yathā deva kaustubha¥ satata¥ hrdi 348  tadvad dāmanakī¥ mālā¥ pūjāñ ca hrdaye vaha
`O Lord, as You always carry a garland of forest flowers and the  Kaustubha jewel on Your chest, so also carry this damanaka garland, and my worship in Your heart'
bhagavanta¥ pranamyātha guru¥ sampūjya bhaktitah 349  sampūjya brāhmanān śaktyā bhuñjita saba bandhubhih
After bowing to the Lord, one should honour the guru with  devotion. After worshipping the brāhmanas as well as one can,  (350-351) one should eat together with friends.
352-353 As said by Brahmā in the Devī Purāna:'O son, in Caitra, etc,  one should perform worship according to the rules with sandalwood pulp, incense, arghya, foodstuffs and garlands of damanaka flowers. With a homa one should worship the Lord to attain all one's desires. Such a man will attain the fruit of bathing  at all holy places:





FROM VILĀSA XV  APPEARANCE OF THE LORD
FESTIVALS DURING  THE NEXT FIVE MONTHS
NIRJALA EKADAŚI
In the Padma Purāna (6.51.15, 19-25):`Bhīmasena said:"Grandfa- 19  ther what should I do, since I am unable to fast? O master, please  describe to me a single vrata which can give plenty of fruits!"
`SrīVyāsa said:"When the sun is in Taurus or Gemini during 20-22  Ekādaśī in the bright fortnight of the month of Jyaistha one
should fast diligently, avoiding water. The wise should avoid water, except when bathing or performing ācamana. Otherwise  one should not taste water, or the fast will be broken. A thoughtful person should zealously avoid water from sunrise to sunrise.  He will attain the fruit of the twelve Dvādaśīs.
DDT: `The twelve Dvādaśīs`: the eight Mahā-dvādaśīs  plus Śayanī-, Pārśva-parivartani- and Bodhinī Dvādaśī,  plus Bhaimī Dvādaśī. Otherwise it may mean the fruit of  all the Dvādaśīs during the twelve months of the year.
"`Then, on the pure morning on Dvādaśī, one should bathe and 23-25  according to the rules give water and gold to the twice born. O
master of the senses, after performing one's duties one should  eat together with brāhmanas. Bhīmasena, please listen to the  merit one gains by doing this. Son, on this day one attains without a doubt the fruit of all the other Ekādaśīs of the year! This  Keśava, the carrier of the conch, disk and club, has told me:"
DDT: The merit is especially great since it is a great effort  to refrain from drinking water in the middle of summer.
Furthermore (6.51.30-33): `Tiger amongst men, when a man 26-28  celebrates this day it brings him wealth, grain, merit, sons, for
tune and happiness. I am telling you the truth! The terrible,  angry messengers of Yama, with enormous, lusty bodies, carrying sticks and ropes, do not bind such a man. That Vaisnava  is at the time of death led to the abode of Visnu by persons  wearing yellow garments, holding conches and disks, fleet as  the mind:
29-31 And also (6.51.39-42): `That foremost of Vaisnavas who  follows the rule of refraining from water gains the merit of ten  million donations of gold with every three hours. The bathing,  giving in charity, muttering of mantras and sacrifices a man  does on this Dvādaśī will all be immortal. This is the statement of Krsna. O king, what shall I say about other observances  than Nirjala Dvādaśī? One who fully fasts and observes the  rules attains the abode of Visnu:
32-34 Similarly: `Bhīmasena, , those who perform this pure  Nirjala Ekādaśī all liberate a hundred relatives. Together with  them he will be led to the temple of Vāsudeva.' And also (6.51.  50): `Those who do not fast on this day commit suicide. They  are full of sin, they behave badly and are evil. There is no doubt  about this: Furthermore (6.51.55): `Both one who listens to this  with devotion and one who declares this to others will attain  heaven. Do not doubt this!'
DDT: The verse beginning with `Those who' shows that  this vrata is mandatory.
THE RULES FOR NIRJALA EKADAŚI
35 yathā prāg-likhita¥ krtvā sañkalpa¥ niyamā¥ vrate  jalam ādāya grhnīyan mantrenānena vaisnavah
After performing the duties explained earlier on, the Vaisnava  should, holding water, state the declaration and the rules for  the vrata with this mantra:
DDT: Having stated the mandatoriness of the vrata he  now writes in the next nine verses about the rules for the
vrata, following the statements of the Uttara-khanda of  the Bhavisya Purāna.'The duties explained earlier oń refers to the rules for Daśamī, etc, that have already been  explained (12.2-22).
THE MANTRA OF RULES
ekādaśyā¥ nirāhāro varjayisyāmi vai jalam 36  keśava-prīnanārthāya atyanta-damanena ca
`To please Keśava I will with great self-restraint fast on Ekādaśī and refrain from water.'
varjayec cāmbv aho-rātra¥ vinā cācamanārthakam 37  vinā ca prāśana¥ pādodakasyātyantapāvanam
One should avoid water during both day and night, except water  for ācamana and water that has washed His feet, for it is greatly  purifying.
DDT: One should refrain from water both during day  and night. In this verse he states that water for ācamana  and bathing and water that has bathed the Lord's feet  should not be avoided, since there will always otherwise  be the fault of impurity. Now, `avoid water, except when  bathing or performing ācamaná was stated earlier (15.21),  but foot-bathing water was not mentioned. The reason is  that it is greatly purifying', it is even more purifying than  ācamana. The mandatoriness of ācamana has been established earlier (3.304-305)•
ekādaśyā¥ niśāyān tu nityapūjā¥ vidhāya hi 38  haimī¥ traivikramī¥ mūrti¥ snāpayet paya-ādibhih
After performing one's prescribed duties in the evening of the  Ekādaśī, one should bathe a golden form of Trivikrama with  milk and so on.
vastrādika¥ samarpyāthābhyarcya gandhādibhiś ca tām 39  pranamyajāgara¥ kuryāt tad-agre nartanādinā
One should offer Him clothes, etc, and worship Him with  sandalwood-paste and so forth. After paying obeisances one  should by dancing and so on keep vigil in front of Him.
40 prātah-snānādi nirvartya ta¥ trivikramam arcayet
One should bathe, etc, in the morning and then worship Trivikrama.
41 śaktyāmbukumbhān viprebhyo dadyād gandhādy-alañkrtān  According to one's means, one should donate to the brāhmanas kumbhas with water, decorated with sandalwood-paste  and so on.
THE CORRESPONDING MANTRA  42 deva-deva hrsīkeśa samsārārnava-tāraka  jalakumbha-pradānena yasyāmi paramā¥ gatim
'God of gods, Hrsīkeśa, rescuer from the ocean of birth and  death! By giving,away this waterpot I will go to the highest  destination:
43 dadyāc ca kanaka¥ chatra¥ vastra yugmam apānakau  jalapātrāni divyāni vibhāve sati vaisnavah
The Vaisnava should donate gold, a parasol, two cloths, sandals or just wonderful waterpots.
44 śaktyā viprān bhojayitvā pītvā bhrātrkarāj jalam  svaya¥ vā pīya maunī san bhuñjīta saha bandhubhih
After feeding the brāhmanas according to one's means, one  should silently drink water from one's brothers hand, or from  oneś own. Then one should eat together with friends.
ŚAYANA DVADAŚI
āsādha-śukla-dvādaśyā¥ harau śiśisyisau sati 45  vaisnavah pārana¥ krtvā saptamudrāś ca dhārayet
On Dvādaśī during the bright fortnight of Asādha, when Hari  wishes to sleep, the Vaisnava should, after breaking the fast,  brand seven marks on his body.
brāhmanah ksatriyo vaiśyah śūdraś caikāntitarddhaye 46  kurvann ātmārpana¥ tapta- mudrābhir deham añkayet
To increase their singlemindedness, brāhmanas, ksatriyas, vaiśyas and śūdras should surrender their self by branding the  body with red-hot marks.
DDT: In this verse he declares that all varnas should  carry the branded marks. This one does to perfect ones  'singlemindednesś or exclusive devotion to the blessed  Lord, like a bull marked with Sivás liñga.`Surrender their  self' or self-surrender is a specific form of devotion. That  also brāhmanas should wear the marks will be duly  elaborated on further on.
In connection with the red-hot marks it is said in the Varāha 47  Purāna: Just to announce their connection, men should carry
the marks of the disk, etc, just like a chaste wife is decorated with  bracelets and so forth'.
DDT: With this statement of Varāha he establishes that  by accepting the red-hot marks one attains the perfection  of singlemindedness. Announcing the ćonnection' means  to declare that one belongs to the Lord. Another reading  says'announce their connection with the Highest Lord'.  The example given is that of a chaste wife who shows that  she has a living husband by carrying bracelets, but who  also wears the ornaments to please her husband. That this  is a sign of devotion is evident.
THE MANDATORINESS OF ACCEPTING
THE MARKS OF THE DISK AND SO ON  48 In the Vāyu Purāna:'To attain the abode of Hari, Vaisnavas of all  varnas should carry the branded marks of the disk and so forth:
DDT: He begins establishing the mandatoriness by the  strenght of the commands in this verse up to verse 59.  Amongst all varnas, the Vaisnava should carry the marks,  because the marks pertain mostly to them. This can be  seen from verse the statement`to perfect his Vaisnavism'  in verse 58. Otherwise, `of all varnas' can be understood in  connection with 'the abode of Hari', the attainment of  which is the perfection of all. Also in this case it is shown  that all varnas should carry the marks.
49-51 In the Brahmānda Purāna: `O king, having fashioned metallic  marks of the disk and so forth, the Vaisnava should brand his  own body.' The Nārada Pañcarātra describes the disk thus:  `One should wear a branded mark of Hari's Sudarśana disk,  hexagonal, having twelve spokes and encircled by three lines:  In the Garuda Purāna, in a discussion between the Lord and  Garuda in connection with the branded marks:'Garuda, this is a  rule for brāhmanas, ksatriyas, vaiśyas and śūdras: for all varnas,  without exeptions:
DDT:`Since the body of a brāhmana never should be injured, this ritual pertains to others than brāhmanaśsuch a doubt should be discarded. This is quite clearly  shown in the verse from the Garuda Purāna and in the  following six verses.
52-55 In the Padma Purāna (6.66.81):As the Agnihotra and studying  the Vedas are mandatory duties for a brāhmana, so is accepting the branded marks of the disk and so on: Furthermore, in  the same book, Uttara-khanda, in a discussion between Śiva  and Umā:`To remove all sin, a brāhmana should brand his upper arms with marks of the conch and disk, heated in a sacrificial fire. He should undertake the brahminical duty of wearing
the five weapons beginning with disk and conch according to  the rules: Also (6.244.40):A brāhmana who does not wear the  disk according to the rules becomes degraded:
Likewise (6.244.41,44): `One should never accept food 56-58  from a brāhmana who has performed thousands of observ
ances, knows all the Uedas and other scriptures, but who does  not wear the disk according to the rules. Such a brāhmana becomes fallen: Moreover (6.244.48-49):'To perfect his śrauta  and smārta duties, and also his mantra, a brāhmana should  mark himself with red-hot brands according to the rules. One  should wear the mark of the disk to attain eligibility for worshipping Hari, to perfect his Vaisnavism, and especially to perfect his devotion:
Also: 'Brāhmanas, and especially Vaisnavas, should wear 59-60  the disk, conch and so forth just like they wear the sacred
tread: In the Srī Sudarśa Sruti (5-6):`One who is truly attentive to the rules of the foremost of the praised ones, makes a  disk with fire. Fire is thousand-spoked, thousand-spoked is the  felly. One whose body is branded with the felly attains sāyujya,  he attains sālokya:
DDT: One who makes a disk with fire attains`sāyujya' or  eternal, close proximity with the Lord and'sālokyá, residence in the world of the Lord. Because of the connection  with fire, there is no fault, rather there is a good quality.  This he shows with the statement beginning with'fire is'.  `Thousand-spoked' means the disk. Fire is purifying while  the disk is most purifying. They are therefore non-different. The implied meaning is that there is no fault in this  ritual, but it is extremely good. Now, since the disk is  present in this one place, wearing the mark is real. This  mark is non-different from the disk itself. This he states  with the phrase`thousand-spoked is the felly'. The`felly' is  the outer rim of the disk, and that mark is indeed the  whole disk itself.
'Who carries the branded disk on his body gets the strength of 61  the gods, of immortal Visnu. Shaking off sin, he proceeds to  heaven, where the ascetics with subdued passions enter.'
DDT:'The strength of the godś means their protection.  `Heaveń is the place where there is no suffering, the highest abode.
62 In the appendix to the Rg Veda:'The raw person whose body  is not branded does not enjoy that. Enjoying together certainly  those who wear completely dwell there. Thus the Yajuh:
DDT: Since their bodies are not branded they are`raw' or  have the intelligence of children. Because of this, they do  not attain `that', the abode beyond words. Instead of énjoying together' another reading (rv 9.83.1) has 'all the  cooked oneś, meaning all those whose bodies are branded.  In the Aśvalāyana-śākhā of the Rg Veda:
63 `Living in the ocean of birth, the best of men,  the ancients, carry on their shoulders and elsewhere  the marks of the lotus and disk of eminent Visnu.
They accept the branded marks of the other weapons:  DDT:`The best of meń means the topmost saints.These  persons are liberated while living, and therefore they are  most ancient of all. That they 'accept' the marks of the  other weapons, such as the club, means that they carry  them also on their bodies.
64 In the appendix to the Chāndogya Upanisad: 'Yajñavalkya  said: "To benefit his self, this man should worship Hari with  love. He should place the marks of the foremost of praised  ones on his limbs with fire. Thus the śruti of Śātātapa:"
In the appendix to the Atharva Veda, in connection with  the branded marks:
65 `With arms branded with Sudarśana,  the devoted gods have gone to heaven.  Marked like this, the Manus create the peoples,
branded, the brāhmanas carry it:  DDT:`It means the disk Sudarśana.
In connection with the branded marks, Śrī Śiva says in the 66  Padma Purāna: 'A brāhmana who is marked with the disk of  Visnu should be worshipped with all rites, but one without the
disk of Visnu should be zealously avoided:
DDT: Having confirmed the mandatoriness through the  orders of scripture by showing the excellence of carrying  these marks, he now establishes it fully by showing that  non-observance will result in sin.'With all riteś means  with śrāddha and so forth.
In the Nārada Purāna, in connection with the branded marks:  'Whose bodies are devoid of the mark of Śrī Krsna's disk like crematoriums are those men or women.
O king, seeing such a person
one should bathe fully dressed and quickly worship Hari!'
bahvaś ca veńkatācārya- pāda-prabhrtibhir budhaih 68  śrutayah srnrtayo 'py atra vikhyātā likhitāh parāh
Wise men such as the honourable Ācārya Ueńkata have in this  connection collected many other famous statements of the śrutí  and smrti.
DDT: Veńkatācārya of the Śrī Sampradāya is foremost  of these knowers of the śruti and smrti. The implied  meaning is that since those statements are widely known  they have not been collected here.
THE FAULT OF NOT  RESPECTING THE MARKS
In the Padma Purāna:`If one happens to see the face of that low- 69  est of men, who having seen the branded mark of the disk blasphemes it, one should look at the suń.
DDT: Now, while the necessity has been established, he  further strenghtens the mandatoriness of this observance
by showing in this verse and the following two the fault of  those who ridicule it through ignorance.
70-71 Also in the Agni Purāna, in the lament of the brāhmana whose  son had been killed by Daśaratha: `Did I consider the form of  Hari as made of stone? Did I at some time see a Vaisnava, whose  body was decorated with branded marks, on the road and disrespect him in my mind? By what deed comes this sorrow over  my son?'
DDT: This is the lament of the brāhmana whose son, by  the name Sravana, had been killed by Daśaratha. This is  the story: Thinking he was an elephant he had chased,  king Daśaratha shot Śravana on hearing him coming. Following the dying son's words, the king brought a pot of water to his blind parents. Worried, the father adressed the  silent Daśaratha.`Śravana! Why did you delay? Why do  you not speak?' He replied:`I am Daśaratha, killer of your  son: Hearing this, the brāhmana fell unconscious, and regaining consciousness after a long time lamented in many  ways.
THE GREATNESS OF WEARING  THE BRANDED MARKS
72-74 In the Garuda Purāna: `Even if someone is impure, badly behaved and has given up all religious duties, if he is marked by  the branded conch and disk he purifies an assembly.' In the  Varāha Purāna, in connection with the branded marks:`Whether  someone decorated with the disk resides in a pure land or one  of barbarians, three yojanas in all directions from him is My  field on earth: In the Brahmānda Purāna:`If a Vaisnava brands  his body with all the weapons of Visnu, he will go to the highest abode:
75-79 Likewise, in the Padma Purāna (6.244.31-34, 37, 38): `One  who wears the pure marks branded with fire on his shoulders  gives up terrible hell and proceeds to the abode of Visnu. One  whose body is branded with a disk kept in a sacrificial fire, attains by this the holy places and sacrifices. There is no doubt
about it! A brāhmana who has marked his shoulders with the  red-hot brand of the disk should mutter his mantra. By this he  will become liberated from birth and death. Those who decorate their shoulders with the branded mark of the disk, all become liberated from sin and attain the highest abode of Visnu:  Furthermore (6.244.55): `Those branded with the disk of  Visnu are spiritual, great souls, but those without the disk of  Visnu are known as materialistic and fallen:
ittham nisedha-vacana¥ nirmūla¥ sad-anādrtam 80  samūla¥ yac ca tat samyag vidhy-abhāvādi-tatparam
Now, the statements prohibiting this observance are baseless  and rejected by the wise, and those statements that are based  on scripture pertain to abandoning the rules, etc.
DDT: Having everywhere settled the wearing of  branded marks, he now skillfully in writing refutes the  statements opposing it. The statements prohibiting this  observance that generally are heard from the Smārtas  are indeed `baseless', because they cannot be found anywhere in old books such as the śrutis, smrtis, Purānas or  Itihāsas. Now, someone may say 'well, in some places  they can be found: To this he replies with `rejected by  the wise', to confirm that such statements are fabricated  by persons connected to wicked Smārtas. Those statements are the talk of madmen, like `to the chaste wife  who does not commit adultery an infirm next birth is  certainly giveń .
Still, in the Brahma-gītā the following clear statement  is given:`O best of the twiceborn, in the age of Kali misled  heretics always carry the marks of the vajra, disk and so  forth on their bodies: This objection he answers with  'those statements that are based on scripturé . The opposing statements based on scripture are aimed at wearing  the marks in a way that is against the rules.'Etć means  that they may also pertain to persons that are not Vaisnavas. This is the meaning of the verse from the Brahmagītā: Since the vajra is also mentioned, wearing the disk  and so forth together with the vajra is forbidden. In this  way the scripturally based statements that prohibit carry
ing the marks should be understood to refer to an incorrect wearing of marks.
Whenever possible, in such scripturally based statements one should try to ascertain the subject. If this is  not possible one should have recourse to understanding  that there is a difference between Vaisnavas and nonVaisnavas in this matter. This is the conclusion.

For wearing the branded marks, one should worship Krsna with  five articles, then the disk and conch. Then one should bow to  them.

THE MANTRA FOR WEARING THE MARKS  sudarśana mahājvāla sūrya-koti-saura-prabhā
ajñānāndhasya me nitya¥ visnor mārga¥ pradarśaya
`Sudarsana, greatly flaming, splendid like ten million suns! Always show me, who am blinded by ignorance, the path of Visnu:  And also:
pāñcajanya nija-dhvāna- dhvasta-pātaka-sañcaya 98  pāhi mām pāpinam ghora- samsārārnava-pātinam
`Pāñcajanya, destroying multitudes of sins by your sound! Please  protect me, a sinner, fallen into the ocean of the terrible cycle  of birth and death:
imam uccārayan mantra¥ daksinādi-kramena tu 99  bhujuyoś cakra-pūrvāni krsna-śastrāni dhārayet
Uttering this mantra, one should one by one place the weapons of Krsna, beginning with the disk, on the right arm and so  forth.
DDT: Arm' means shoulder. `Beginning with the disk':  first one should place the disk and then the others such as  the conch. About this he writes `on the right arm and so  forth'. First one should mark the right shoulder, then the  left, and so on. The specific details will be given in a quotation from the Varāha Purāna below (15.103-104).
kalatrādi parīvārān nijān sarvāmś ca vaisnavah 100  bhagavaty arpayan tapta- mudrābhis tābhir añkayet
Offering them to the Lord, the Vaisnava should brand his wife,  etc, companions and everything with these red-hot marks.  DDT:`Offering' means presenting with the mentality`they  belong to you'. As it is said in the Śrīmad Bhāgavatam  (11.3.28): `Wives, sons, homes, life airs: all this is an offer
ing to the Highest'. The offering of wife, etc, should be  done one after another.'These' refer to the worshipped  forms of the disk and so forth.
As it said in the Varāha Purāna:`With red-hot brands one should 101-104  place marks on one's own shoulders, the wife, children, servants,
animals and on oneś wealth: Also:`Having out of iron fashioned  marks of the five weapons according to the rules, the knower of
mantras should place them, one by one with their respective  mantra. On the forehead one should wear the club, on the top of  the head the bow and arrow, the sword Nandaka in the middle of  the chest and the disk and conch on the arms: Furthermore: A  brāhmana should wear Sudarśana on his right arm and the  conch on his left. This is the knowledge of knowers of Brahman:
DDT: `Iroń denotes also gold and so forth, as will be seen  further on (15.105). Since the bow and arrow are companions, they are counted as one. In this way there are five  weapons.
THE MATERIAL OF THE MODELS  OF THE DISK AND SO FORTH
105 In the Navapraśna Pañcarātra:'Having fashioned a disk of gold,  silver, copper, brass or iron, the wise man should brand himself  in the proper way'.
106 evam eva prabodhanyā¥ dvādaśyā¥ bhagavat-paraih  tapta-mudrā dhruva¥ dhāryā dvārakāya¥ viśesatah

DDT:'In Dvārakā': because of the special strength of the  disk in its own holy place, or because there is a special  greatness in accepting branded marks there.
THE FESTIVAL OF LYING DOWN  ON THE OCEAN OF MILK
 107 tato nīrājya krsnan tu narayānena vaisnavah  samam gitādi ghosena nayet punya¥ jalaśayam

atha puspāñjali¥ dattvā yānād uttārya ca prabhum 108  samprārthya hasta¥ dattvā ca tīre samupaveśayet

After performing ācamana, one should with clean body and  hands utter the declaration, perform nyasa on oneself and the  Lord, and then bathe Him according to the rules.
DDT: One should state a suitable declaration following  the ones given earlier on.
samprārthya jala-madhye ta¥ deva¥ samsnāpayet sukham 110  gandha-puspādibhiś cātha mahāpūjā¥ samācaret
One should offer prayers and then happily bathe the Lord in  the water. Then one should perform opulent worship with  sandalwood-paste, flowers, and so on.
DDT: One should offer prayers like 'All glory to Mahāvisnu! Please protect the world!'
THE MANTRA FOR SLEEP
śese paryañka-varye śmin phanā-mani ganāmale m  śvetadvīpāntare deva kuru nidrā¥ namo śtv iti
`O Lord, in the middle of Svetadvīpa, please fall asleep on the  eminent couch of Śesa with unlimited pure bejewelled hoods:  THE MANTRA OF PRAYER
supte tvayi jagannātha jagat supta¥ bhaved idam 112  vibuddhe tu vibudhyeta prasanno me bhavācyuta
'Lord of the universe, when You sleep, the whole world sleeps;  when you awake, it also awakes. Be pleased with me, Infallible  one!'
113 ity āśasya prabhor agre grhnīyān niyama¥ vratī  caturmāsesu kartavya¥ krsna-bhakti-vivrddhaye
After praying like this in front of the Lord, the vrata-performer  should accept some restrictions for the four months of the  rainy period to increase his devotion to Krsna.
DDT: Why should a Vaisnava accept restrictions during  the rainy period? He gives the answer with'to increase his  devotion to Krsna: One incurs sin by not, and also gains a  special thing by doing so, devotion. This is the conclusion.  PAVITRAROPANA DVADAŚI
śravanasya site pakse dvādaśyā¥ vaisnavair mudā  kartavyah krsnadevasya pavitrāropanotsavah
168 On Dvādaśī during the bright fortnight of Śravana Vaisnavas  should happily perform the festival of offering Lord Krsna a cord.  MANDATORINESS OF THE FESTIVAL
169-yo In the appendix to the Rg Ueda: `One who makes a cord has  bathed in all holy places and been initiated into all sacrifices.  He becomes dear to Hari. The demons will steal away the fruit  of a whole year of worship, etc, of one who does not perform  the festival according to the rules given in the scriptures:
DDT: First he shows that the festival is mandatory since  it is dear to Krsna, and then with the next three verses  (yo-ya) he shows that it is also mandatory since nonperformance will result in sin.'Etć means muttering mantras, sacrifices and so on.
y In the Yoga-sāra, in the story of the birth of the cord, Rudra gives  this boon to Pavitra, the king of snakes:`The fruit of muttering
mantras, sacrifices and so on will be destroyed for those who do  not think much of you, who are so respected by me:
DDT: The story of the cord: A great snake by the name  Srī Pavitra, a brother of Vāsuki, king of snakes, worshipped the blessed Śiva with devotion until he became  pleased. Then he asked him for the following benediction:"May I become an ornament around your neck:' Śiva  was greatly pleased and said: "Become an ornament  around the necks of all the gods! All their devotees  should also fashion a cord with your form and offer it to  their own god. Otherwise they will incur a great sin:'
In the Visnu-rahasya:`O best of sages, a whole year of worship 172-173  will become fruitless for one who does not offer the cord ac
cording to the rules. Therefore, men who are devoted to Visnu  should year after year offer the cord with devotion to Hari:  DDT: `Year after year' means that since it is continual it is  mandatory,just like it is said that one should'spring after  spring sacrifice with light. Here it is also shown that it is  mandatory for those who are devoted to Visnu', Vaisnavas.
THE GREATNESS OF OFFERING THE CORD  Baudhāyana says: As long as one honours the cord, one's dura- 174-176  tion of life, freedom from disease and majesty will all abundantly
increase: In the Mahā-sarñhitā: `O twice-born one, the worship  that a brāhmana has performed during a year is completed by  the offering of the cord. Thus spoke Lord Hari: In the Visnurahasya:`Offering the cord to Visnu brings enjoyment, liberation,  fame for woman and man, merit, happiness, glory and riches:
DDT:'Fame for woman and mań means fame for both  husband and wife, or then for both women and men. It  indicates that offering the cord to Visnu is meant also for  Vaisnava women.
`It is the merit of all merits, indeed a destroyer of all sin. There- 177-178  fore offering the cord is known as most pure. The fruit one at
tains by devotedly fully worshipping Janārdana during a whole  year, one attains by simply offering the cord!'
179-180 And also: `Since it causes sin to disappear and orders the  cutting of attachment to matter, it is called cord. It is known as  the effulgence of Brahman. It is known by the name of Visnu  among the people. It is indeed the Lord of sacrifices, the Lord  of rites in the form of a thread:
DDT: Here he gives an etymology for the word ćord'. In  the following two verses he wishes to show a special  greatness of the cord: the Blessed Lord who wears a garland of forest flowers, and so on, is non-different from his  secondary members.
181 `That threefold thread is called Nārāyana. It is known as the self  of the three gods, three Uedas and three-lettered syllable Aum'.  DDT: The`threefold thread' consists of three threads. The  reason for this is then given: it is the self of Brahmā, Visnu
and Śiva, etc. Even though the cord is eternally liberated in  the world of Vaikuntha by its being a decoration of the  Lord, with regard to Śrī Maheśvara, it appears as a decoration on the form of the Lord, in the form of a threefold  thread made by Vaisnavas with special devotion, just like  the Lord appears in an installed image. This is the understanding. Therefore the mantra for installation is:
visnulokāt pavitrādyāgaccha
`O cord, please today come from the world of Visnu!` (15.207)  182 tatra baudhāyanādy-uktah pavitrāropane vidhih  sammato vidusā¥ krsnārcane yo `tra sa likhyate
The rules for offering the cord have been explained in the writings of Baudhāyana and others. Here those rules for worshipping Krsna that all the knowers have agreed on are noted.
DDT: Because of different disciplic successions and  schools there are many different rules. The rules of those  who are conversant with the scriptures are written here.
RULES FOR OFFERING THE CORD
sauvarrtai rājatais tāmraih ksaumaih sūtrais tu pādmikaih 183  kārpāsair vā pavitrānīsyante kāśaih kuśair api
One should fashion strings of gold, silver, copper, silk, lotus fibres, cotton or kuśa grass (Saccharum Spontaneum).
DDT: These materials are listed in order of preference.
tatra kārpāsika¥ sūtra¥ brāhmanī-kartita¥ śubham 184  ānīya trigunī-krtya punas trigunayet śucih
If the thread is of cotton, it should be fine and woven by a  brāhmanī. After getting the thread, a pure person should make  it threefold, and then threefold again.
DDT:`Brāhmanī' means a virgin daughter of a brāhmana  or a widow full of good qualities, but not a śūdra or someone with bad behaviour.`Fine' means that it should be excellent and not be too thick.'A pure persoń means someone who is pure by having taken bath, etc.
pañca gavyena tat proksya praksālya śucināmbunā 185  mūlenascottaraśatam mantrenāthābhimantrayet
It should be sprinkled with the five substances of the cow (milk,  yoghurt, ghee, cow dung and cow urine) and then with pure  water. Then one should recite 108 root-mantras over it.
trīni sāstaśatenāsya tasyārdhenāsya cārdhatah 186  jānūrunābhidaghnāni pavitrāny ācaret prabhoh
One should fashion three cords for the Lord, having 108, half  of that and again half of that threads and reaching to the  knees, thighs and navel.
DDT: A Vaisnava with a sacred thread should in a pure  place tie three cords one by one: a large, a middle and a  small one. The large one should consist of 108 nine-fold  threads, the middle one of half of that, 5q, and the small
one of 27. The lenght for the large is that it should reach  to the knees of the form of the Lord, the middle one to  the thighs and the small one to the navel.
187 sattri¥śad granthayas tesām ādye kāryās tu madhyame  caturvi¥śair ante ca dvādaśa granthayo budhaih
A wise person should make 36 knots on the first one, 24 on the  middle and 12 on the last.
DDT: One should tie the knots at equal distances. The  `first' corresponds with the large, the `last with the small.  188 arigustha-parva-mātrān tu kuryād granthim athottame
tad-ardha¥ madhyame kuryāt tad-ardhañ ca kanīyasī
One should leave a distance of one thumb between each knot  on the large, half of that one the middle one, and half of that  on the small one.
DDT:`One thumb' indicates the lenght of a thumb of the  form of the Lord so that a small form also gets a small  cord, and since different worshippers will have thumbs of  different lenghts anyway.
189 granthīh kurvīta sarvatra suvrttān sumanoharān  na vai visama-sańkhyākān granthīn kurvīta kutracit
The knots should everywhere be made beautifully round and enchanting. One should, however, never make an uneven number  of knots.
DDT: `Everywhere means on all the cords. `Never' refers  to the cords of the associates, etc.
190 astottara-sahasrena tat-sūtrasya pavitrakam  astottaraśata granthi- vana-mālākhyam ācaret
One should make a cord called Vanamālā with 1oo8 threads  and 108 knots.
191 ārabhya mukuta¥ yā tu sūtrair viracitā śubhā  āpādalambinī mālā vanamālā prakīrtitā
p beautiful garland made of threads, beginning at the crown  and reaching down to the feet, is called a Vanamālā.
kuryād gandha-pavitrañ ca sūtrair dvādaśahhih śubhaih 192  aratni pranita¥ tac ca dvādaśa-granthika¥ krtī
One should fashion a perfume-cord of twelve splendid threads,  reaching from the elbow to the little finger and having twelve  knots.
DDT: This cord of nine-fold thread is meant for applying  perfume.
pavitrāni parivāra- devatānā¥ samācaret I93  sūtrais tair udusańkhyākaih kalāsańkhyārka-sańkhyakaih

DDT: One should tie three cords for the associate divinities also, one large, one medium and one small.
tesu granthīn yathāśobha¥ baddhvā vahner guror api I94  saptavi¥śatibhih sūtraih sadvi¥śatibhir ātmanah
On them one should tie knots to create a beautiful appearance.  For the fire and the guru one should make cords of 27 threads,  and to oneself of 26.
yathāsambhavam anyesā¥ pavitrāni ca kārayet I95  sampādayec ca sarvāni śobhanāny eva yatnatah
As far as possible, one should have cords made for others also.  One should endeavour to make all of them beautiful.

vastrenācchādya patale sthāpayet tāni vainave

DDT: And so oń refers to substances such as camphor. If  one is unable to use these, one can also simply use ku¥ku­ ma, or íf one is unable to use even that, turmeric and so on.  198 krtvā krtya¥ daśamyāñ ca pavitrāropanāya hi
krsna¥ vijñāpya tad-rātri¥ yathā prāg-likhita¥ nayet
After performing one's duties on Daśamī, one should inform  Krsna of the offering of the cord, and then spend the night as  previously described.
DDT: Now he describes the observances for the three  days of the festival of offering the cord. He begins with  Daśamī.As previously described' means as was explained  in the section dealing with rules for Daśamī (13.2-18).  That basically means to eat only once, give up the use of a  tooth-twig and instead clean the teeth by doing ācamana  twice, perform the rituals at dusk and then worship the  Lord. After offering a handful of flowers, one should declare the following to the Lord:
tava yāga¥ karisye `ha¥ pavitra-mayam acyuta  āmantrito `si bhagavan parivāra yuto mayā
`I will perform the sacrifice of the cord to You, Infallible  One. Together with Your associates, You are invited by  me, Lord!'
After praying like this, one should spend the night as  earlier described (13.22) by observing brahmacārya and  sleeping on the ground, and so on.
Now, some are of the opinion that one should spend  the night of Daśamī, perform the duties for the morning  of Ekādaśī, and only then declare the offering of the cord  as mentioned above. Then one should arrange the paraphernalia for offering the cords as well as one is able and  bow to the guru. In his house and on his order one should  then fashion the cords. The activities such as fashioning  the cords on this Ekādaśī should be understood to pertain to those who have the means.
I99 ekādaśyā¥ prabhāte ca nitya-krtya¥ samāpya hi  devālayam upaskrtya mandala¥ racayet śubham
Having performed the morning duties on Ekādaśī, one should  decorate the temple and construct a beautiful mandala.
DDT: In this verse and upto verse 224 he describes the  duties on Ekādaśī.`The morning dutieś refer to bathing  and so on. One should decorate the temple with ointments, canopies, etc. The'beautiful mandala' refers to mandalas such as the Sarvatobhadra.
In the opinion of some, this can be added: `One should  first worship the doorkeepers and then enter the sacrifical  arena. One should then make a braid out of 36 blades of  darbha-grass with the length from elbow to the tip of the  middle finger, and purify it with root-mantras and the  five substances of the cow Then one should perform bhūta-śuddhi (purification of the elements), smear the braid  with the five substances of a cow and sprinkle the whole  sacrificial arena with it. After this, one should bow to the  guru and then, following one's own rulebooks, prepare  nyāsa-water, mutter the Nrsi¥ha root-mantra (ksrau¥)  over some mustard seeds and scatter them in the ten directions. One should consider them to form a wall all  around.
`Then one should according to the rules please a wellbehaved Vaisnava, learned in the Uedas and Uedāńgas,  who will perform the sacrifice. He should, according to  the rules of the scriptures and those pertaining to the particular house, offer a8 or 1o8 oblations and pour the leftover ghee into the throw-out pot to bless the cord. Then  the sacrificer should perform nyāsa following the rules,  and after performing this occasional elaborate worship,  begin the great worship pertaining to the festival of offering the cord:
krtvā krsnasya nityārca¥ pavitrāropanārthakam 200  pūjā¥ viśesatah krtvā krsna¥ vyāpayed idam

RULES FOR REMOVING THE CORDS
In the Tantras According to time, place and circumstances, the 235-237  Lord should carry the cords made of strings a month, a fort
night, three nights or one day and night. At the time of bathing, they should be removed. They should be sprinkled with  water and then again placed on the Lord. At the end, the Lord  should be especially worshipped with flowers and sandalwood  pulp, offered different kinds of foodstuffs, and then the cords  should be removed with this mantra:
o¥ samvatsarī¥ śubhā¥ pūjā¥ sampādya vidhivan mama 238  vrajedānī¥ pavitra tva¥ visnu-loka¥ visarjitam
`Om. O cord, having made my yearly worship conform to the  rules and auspicious, now you will be removed. Return to the  abode of Visnu!'
yāvad deve pavitrāni tāvat tisthet samāhitah 239  brahmacārī havisyāśī deva-pūjā-parāyanah
As long as the Lord wears the cords, one should concentratedly  live in celibacy, eat only havisya and be devoted to the worship of  the Lord.
THE FRUIT OF THE VRATA
240 As said in the work of Baudhāyana:`One who thus follows all  the rules and acts like this year after year, will no doubt attain  to the highest abode, where dwells the Man-lion'.
PARŚVA-PARIVARTANA DVADAŚI  543 bhadrasya śukla-dvādaśyā¥ śayanotsavavat prabhoh  kali-dānotsava¥ kuryād vaisnavaih saha vaisnavaih
On Dvādaśī in the bright fortnight of Bhadra, a Vaisnava should  together with Vaisnavas celebrate the festival of turning over,  just like the festival of the Lord's going to sleep.
544-545 In the Uttara-khanda of the Bhavisya Purāna:`When Ekādaśī in the bright fortnight of the month of Bhadra arrives,  Visnu turns over. It destroys great sin. Having led the Lord to  the bank of a reservoir of water, and having fully worshipped  Him, one should turn Him over on His right side:
DDT: Even though the Uttara-khanda of the Bhavisya  Purāna says`Ekādaśī', it should be understood as'Dvādaśī'.  The statement of the Uttara-khanda of the Bhavisya Purāna should be understood to teach the non-difference of  Ekādaśī and Dvādaśī.
`One should turn Him over' means that earlier He  slept on His left side, but from now on He sleeps on His  right side.
THE MANTRA OF REQUESTING  546 deva deva jagannātha yogīgamya nirañjana  katidānam kurusvādya māsi bhadrapade śubhe

THE GREATNESS OF ŚRAVANA DVĀDAŚI
māsi bhadrapade śuklā dvādaśī śravanānvitā 549  mahatī dvādaśī jñeyā upavāse mahāphalā
arcayitvācyuta¥ bhaktyā labhet punya¥ daśābdikam
Dvādaśī connected with Sravana during the bright fortnight of  the month of Bhadra is called Mahatī Dvādaśī. Fasting during  that time is greatly meritorious.One who worships the Infallible  one with devotion at that time attains the merit of ten years.
DDT:`The merit of ten yearś means the merit one gains  by worshipping the Lord during ten years.
phala¥ datta-hutānāñ ca tasyā¥ laksa guna¥ bhavet 550  The fruit of of donations and sacrifices is multiplied by a hun
dred thousand on this day.
In the Skanda Purāna: Dvādaśī in the bright fortnight of 551-554  the month of Bhadra combined with Śravana is known as Ma
hatī Dvādaśī. Fasting on this day brings great merit. One who  fasts and bathes in an auspicious confluence of rivers on this  day gains the fruit of twelve Dvādaśīs. If this day also falls on a  Wednesday, its is Atyanta-mahatī Dvādaśī, and whatever given  in charity on that day becomes imperishable. The fruit of donations and sacrifices is multiplied by a hundred thousand on  this day.'
555-556 In the Brahma-vaivarta Purāna, in a conversation between  a father and son:`When the day of Hari during the bright fortnight of Bhadra is combined with Śravana and falls on a Wednesday, the worshippable Vāmana fulfills all pure desires in  one's mind. The confluence of all rivers appear in a confluence  on that day.
557-560 `Ekādaśī in the bright fortnight of Bhadra leads to heaven,  in the dark to destruction of sin. In Phālguna it liberates men  even from the sin of killing a brāhmana. This glorious tithi,  however, bestows great merit at a confluence. It destroys all the  sins of those who celebrate it: And also: All the holy places  meet at a confluence, and all the gods congregate on earth during this glorious day. In this way this secret of all the Purānas  is told. One who worships Vāmana at a confluence will not be  born as a ghost:
561-562 In the Visnu-dharmottara Purāna (1.60.1-3): `Srī Paraśurāma said:"Is there any way in which those who are unable  to fast can by just one day of fasting gain great fruit? Great  god, fixed in vratas, please tell me that!" Srī Sañkara replied:"O  Rāma, knower of duties, one who fasts, bathes and worships  Janārdana on Mahatī Dvādaśī combined with the asterism  Śravana, easily attains the fruit of the twelve Dvādaśīs!"'
563-566 Furthermore (1.60.5-8): `Rāma, when Dvādaśī combined  with Sravana falls on a Wednesday, it is called Atyanta-mahatī  Dvādaśī. O descendant of Bhrgu, bathing, muttering mantras,  sacrificies, charity, Śrāddha-ceremonies and worship of the  Lord lead all to liberation on this day. Rāma, one who bathes  in any confluence on that day without a doubt attains the fruit  of bathing in the Gangā. During Śravana all confluences al
ways award enormous merit, and especially so on Dvādaśī,  and even more so when combined with a Wednesday.'
In the Uttara-khanda of the Bhavisya Purāna, Yudhisthira 567-570  says (4.75.1-4): `O Highest Lord, Sinless One, please tell me
about one meritorious Dvādaśī for those who are not able to  always fast: Śrī Krsna replied:"Dvādaśī together with Śravana  in the bright fortnight of Bhadra bestows all pleasures. The  merit of fasting at that time is very great. One who fasts and  bathes at the confluence of rivers attains the fruit of bathing in  the Gañgā. Do not doubt this! When Dvādaśī combined with  Sravana falls on a Wednesday, it is called Atīva-mahatī. Everything given away on that day becomes eternal: "
Also, in the same book, in the story of the merchant 57I-574  (4.75.68-71):At the connection of Śravana and Dvādaśī he wor

Having reached that land, the  greatly fortunate merchant, bedecked with ornaments of pure  gold, happily enjoyed in the company of divine ladies for a  whole kalpa:

A Dvādaśī in Bhadra that  falls on a Wednesday and even half the time is connected with  Sravana, is called Jayā by the sages. One who with great endeavour fully fasts on that day attains mystic abilities and  perfection:

DDT: Here he gives the special mantras and mode of  worship. Buddha and Kalki should be worshipped as one  person on all the limbs, since they differ from the others  by uprooting the deceit of men. For this reason they are  listed as a pair. In the opinion of some others, the two  Rāmas should be grouped together. In this manner the  rules for worship are quite diverse. One should follow  those taught in one's own disciplic succession.

Then one should prepare food with ghee mixed ín yoghurt according to the rules. First one should offer it to the brāhmanas,  and then one should oneself eat together with friends.

One who does all  this with faith will attain the fruit:
THE GREATNESS OF THIS VRATA  654-656 In the same book: `For one who performs this vrata on the day  of Vijayā in the age of Kali, nothing is difficult to attain, neither in this world nor in the next. A great man who gives away  the fruit of this vrata to his ancestor is a saviour of the family.  From the position of an ancestor or even from debt one attains  liberation. Nothing more purifying than this is known, nothing equal or greater than the Vijayā-vrata described here:

As on Śayana, one should perform a festival at the ocean of milk  on this day. After awakening Krsna and fully worshipping Him  according to the rules, He should be placed on a cart.
THE MANDATORINESS OF PRABODHANI
In the Skanda Purāna it is said: All the merit a man on earth 274  has acquired since birth becomes useless if he does not celebrate
the day of awakening.'
DDT: This verse is meant to indicate the mandatoriness  of also the chariot festival and so on.
THE GREATNESS OF PRABODHANI
In the same book (2.4.33.1-8):`The greatness of Prabodhanī 275-279  destroys sin and increases one's merit. It bestows liberation
upon the intelligent performers. Listen, best of the sages!  Until Hari-bodhanī in Kārttika, the burner of sin, appears,  Bhāgirathī Gańgā is useless on earth, o best of the brāhmanas. Until the tithi of Visnu, Hari-bodhanī, comes in Kārttika, all the holy places, oceans and lakes are useless. A man  who fasts on one Prabodhanī attains the fruit of a thousand  Vājapeya-sacrifices and a hundred horse sacrifices! O brāhmana, no matter how difficult oneś desire is to fulfil in the  three worlds of moving and non-moving creatures, Haribodhanī awards it:
280-282 `O brāhmana, even to someone who fasts simply in sport  Hari-bodhanī affords opulence, progeny, merit, majesty and  happiness. Powerful sins, great as mount Meru, Hari-bodhanī  burns up by one's fasting even once. Whatever fruit one can attain by giving all kinds of charity on earth, that Hari-bodhanī  awards by one's fasting even once:
283-286 Furthermore:`Best of sages, one who performs Prabodhanī  in Kārttika awakens his good fortune. By this his family is indeed cleansed. Whatever holy places there are in the three  worlds all reside in the house of one who performs Prabodhanī! Give up all duties and please the carrier of the disk by  fully fasting on Hari-bodhanī Ekādaśī in Kārttika. O sage, what  is the use of many observances leading to higher worlds for  one who fasts on Hari-bodhanī in Kārttika?
DDT: The`higher worlds' are useless since they also bring  the misery of birth and death.
287-289 `One who fasts on Hari-bodhanī is a knower, a yogi, an ascetic.  He has control over his senses. He will attain heaven and liberation. This tithi is dearest to Visnu, a giver of the essence of  religion. A man who fasts on this day once attains liberation.  One who fasts on Prabodhanī will never again enter a womb.  O Nārada, therefore, give up all kinds of religion and do this!
290-292 `O brāhmana, that bathing, giving in charity, austerity or  sacrifice that is done by men in honour of Janārdana on Prabodhanī becomes immortal. O son, this day of Visnuś awakening is a great vrata, a destroyer of heaps of enormous sins. One  should fully fast at that time according to the rules. One who  has satisfied Janārdana, Lord of gods, goes splendidly to the  abode of Hari, illuminating all the directions:
293 Also, in the Padma Purāna:`The unlimited Lord, the rider  of Garuda, fulfils all the desires of those who fast with undivided minds on the day when He wakes up from His sleep on  the bed of serpents in the ocean of milk:
294-299 In the Varāha Purāna :`O fair-eyed one, one who is not generally able to fast should fast fully on one meritorious Dvādaśī,
Prabodhanī. Having worshipped the Lord of all, the Master of  the masters of the universe, one attains the whole fruit of twelve  Dvādaśīs. Dear one, if this tithi is combined with Uttarabhadra  and falls on a Tuesday, its merit is multiplied unlimited times!  Beautiful one, men who fast according to the custom on Śayanī or Bodhanī go to my residence along with millions of gifts.  Sweet one, if this Ekādaśī is combined with Uttarabhadra and  falls on a Monday in the month of Kārttika, it is called"Unlimited".Anything done then becomes unlimited! The fruit of that  Unlimited day is likewise unlimited merit!'
In the same book, in a conversation between Yama and Nā- 300-301  rada:`O sage, now I will tell you something else, the most secret

THE SPECIAL GREATNESS OF
PERFORMING THE VRATA IN MATHURA
In the Padma Purāna: As long as Bodhanī, dear to Visnu, is 302-304  not performed in Mathurā, the holy places and sacrifices such

Such persons on the path of material life should indeed  perform this Prabodhanī. Fool! Why should it then not be celebrated in Mathurā? What is the use of anything else?'
DDT:'Anything else refers to other deeds or holy places.  THE SPECIAL GREATNESS OF  WORSHIPPING THE LORD
